    fixture backtest through the real engine, bundles the 7 artifacts into a BacktestRecord, and
    durably persists via save_to_path. LOAD-MODIFY-SAVE: loads existing history first and accumulates
    (no demo-pair clobber); default-pair seed is idempotent; --run-id persists one labeled run and
    fails closed on a duplicate run id. Results dir from --dir else ATP_BACKTEST_RESULTS_DIR (the
    Phase-1 config key, read as env var) else fail closed. Missing dir fails closed unless --init
    (symmetric with query's load), so an unmounted/typoed path can't fork a fresh history.
  * query [--dir D] [--strategy S] [--from T --to T] [--completed-from T --completed-to T]
    [--param k=v]... [--full]: load_from_path -> RecordQuery (all 3 axes + combined) -> prints each
    matching record's 7 artifacts; --full renders the COMPLETE trade log + equity curve (every interior
    fill/equity mark recoverable, not just first/last).

Design headline — the SRS-EXE-001 facets made falsifiable:
- Single-live authority OWNED by the execution engine (AGENTS.md "live-only IB enforcement"): the
  canonical LiveDesignation is a private field reached only via designate/demote/route_order — no caller
  can supply a forged authority at the routing boundary.

  StrategyMode; NotDesignated -> NON_LIVE_STRATEGY_SUBMISSION BEFORE any broker/connectivity/freshness

Design notes (the headline is FALSIFIABILITY + the three named artifacts):
- The SRS-BT-010 criterion is literally a repeated-run equality test: "repeated runs produce identical
  trade logs, equity curves, AND metrics; parallelism, floating-point ordering, and platform random
  values do not introduce nondeterminism." The engine + every sibling module already CLAIM determinism;
  what was missing was a comparable, falsifiable artifact. This module supplies it:
  (1) RunDigest = an opaque u64 FNV-1a fingerprint, domain-tagged ATP-BACKTEST-RUN-DIGEST,
      `run-digest:{hex}` Display. digest_result folds the BacktestResult (data_source, range,
      bars_processed, each Fill field, each EquityPoint, final_equity) as EXACT i64 minor units —
      encode_result_body carries NO f64 / to_bits, so the money path has no float-formatting
      nondeterminism (and no money-correctness leak). digest_run additionally folds the eight
      PerformanceMetrics ratios through their exact f64::to_bits payload (push_opt_f64) + the benchmark
      symbol, with a has_metrics domain-separation flag, so the fingerprint spans all THREE named
      artifacts and a run-with-metrics can never alias a run-without. digest_result == digest_run(r, None).
  (2) runs_match / metrics_match return the FIRST divergence as a LOCALIZED DeterminismError
      (TradeLog{index} / EquityCurve{index} / lengths / FinalEquity / BarsProcessed / Metrics{metric}),
      metrics compared via to_bits so a +0.0/-0.0 or NaN-bit difference is caught — not smoothed over.
  (3) verify_reproducible runs the engine TWICE over identical inputs (building a fresh strategy each
      replay via an FnMut factory, since BacktestStrategy is &mut), asserts runs_match AND digest
      equality (the DeterminismError::Digest cross-check is defense for any BacktestResult field
      runs_match does not yet cover), and surfaces a replay that does not complete as Run(BacktestError).
- DETERMINISM DISCIPLINE: the verifier is itself deterministic (fixed left-to-right byte fold, total-
  order field encoding, no parallelism/RNG/clock) — it honors the property it checks. The 64-seed
  property sweep proves bit-identical output on re-run AND under SOURCE-ITERATION-ORDER SHUFFLE (the
  engine stable-sorts the replay window, so a shuffled catalog yields the same digest — the criterion's
  "ordering does not introduce nondeterminism" analog). The falsifiability test injects a strategy that
  reads a counter shared ACROSS runs and confirms verify_reproducible CATCHES it (TradeLog{index:0}).
- NUMERIC/CODEC BOUNDARY: reuses the proven backtest_store.rs FNV-1a + length-prefixed + to_bits codec,
  mirrored LOCALLY in determinism.rs (each sibling module carries its own small encoders) rather than
  refactoring shared helpers out of backtest_store.rs — that would be unrelated-module churn. Reads the
  existing backtest::{BacktestResult,Fill,EquityPoint} + metrics::PerformanceMetrics types only; the
  digest is ADDITIVE (no logic touched in backtest.rs/metrics.rs/backtest_store.rs).
- HOME = atp-simulation (SRS-BT-003 co-locates the backtest engine with the sim engine; the digest reads
  the engine's own output). Deps stay atp-strategy-engine + atp-types only — NO broker/execution/
  orchestrator dependency; dependency direction clean.

     family over IMMUTABLE inputs (no shared mutable state in any ordering) + lib doc fix (fix 276f26e). THE

Design notes (the headline is the THREE-DELIVERABLE numeric surface + the determinism discipline):
- The tear-sheet bundles exactly the three SYS-18 names. (1) IC = per-period Spearman rank
  correlation between factor value and forward return: average tie ranks (average_ranks) -> Pearson
  of the ranks (pearson) -> CLAMPED to the [-1,1] domain (the BT-009-R5-style domain bound Codex
  cares about; FP can overflow a rank-Pearson to 1.0000002). A period with zero rank dispersion
  (constant factor OR constant returns) yields None — the per_period series is Vec<(u64,Option<f64>)>,
  never a fabricated zero. mean/std/risk-adjusted IC (the IC information ratio) aggregate over the
  DEFINED ICs only. (2) Factor returns: securities sorted into `quantiles` buckets by the total order
  (factor_value, SecurityKey); quantile_of(pos,count,Q) = pos*Q/count gives buckets that differ in
  size by at most one and are ALL non-empty when count>=Q (validated); the spread is top mean - bottom
  mean (the dollar-neutral long-short period return), so cumulative_spread is the COMPOUNDED
  Pi(1+spread)-1. (3) Turnover: 1 - |current ∩ previous|/|current| churn of the top and bottom
  quantile between consecutive periods (denominator = current quantile size).
- NUMERIC BOUNDARY (mirrors metrics.rs doctrine): factor scores and returns are dimensionless f64
  — this is the factor domain, NOT a money-correctness leak (no integer-minor money enters this
  module). Determinism (the SRS-BT-010 criterion): fixed left-to-right folds, total-order tie breaks,
  no parallelism/RNG/clock; the property sweep proves bit-identical output under re-run AND under
  per-period observation reversal.
- TRUST BOUNDARY (fail-closed FactorPanel::validate): non-empty panel; quantiles>=2; each period
  non-empty with finite factor/return; strictly increasing period ts; no duplicate SecurityKey in a
  period; each period holds >= quantiles securities. The runtime_services.json trust_boundary tokens
  are the CONSTRUCTION form (Err(FactorAnalysisError::X) so the check verifies validate actually
  RAISES each — the bare-variant form was non-unique because the validate construction site precedes
  the enum decl in file order; this also made the L3/L7 negative-mutation tests meaningful).
- HOME = atp-factor-pipeline (the AGENTS.md-named owner; deps atp-data + atp-types only). The three
  deliverables are self-contained numerics, so NO atp-simulation dependency was introduced —
  dependency direction stays clean. Reuses atp_types::SecurityKey (Eq/Hash/Ord) as the security id.

POST-REVIEW HARDENING (the value of the REAL adversarial layer — the user DID then run
/codex:adversarial-review; the first run scoped the whole branch and tripped refusal-clause #4 on
the SAFETY_PATH_RE prep, so it was re-run with --base 860df19 to scope just the feat; that pass
returned needs-attention with TWO high findings, both VALID and both fixed before the feature is
considered done — fix commit on top of the feat):
  R1 [high] "Middle quantile means can leak infinity into a successful tear sheet": validate()
     allows any finite f64, but a bucket mean is an unchecked sum, so two near-f64::MAX returns in a
     MIDDLE bucket overflow its mean to +inf while finite top/bottom buckets give a finite spread —
     compute_tear_sheet then returned Ok with inf in per_quantile_mean, contradicting the fail-closed
     finiteness claim (I only guarded the spread + aggregates, not the per-bucket means). FIX: guard
     every quantile mean through finite("quantile_mean") -> NonFiniteComputation. Regression:
     infinity_in_a_middle_quantile_fails_closed (L1) + extreme_returns_in_a_quantile_fail_closed
     (integration + L7 behavioral).
  R2 [high] "Security-key tie breaking fabricates returns for constant factors": equal factor values
     are split across quantiles by the SecurityKey tiebreak, so a constant (or cutoff-tied) factor
     still got bottom/top portfolios and a non-zero spread driven purely by security identity — false
     alpha — even though the IC correctly reported None. This was an INCONSISTENCY with my own
     "undefined-not-fabricated" doctrine (careful for IC, not for the spread). FIX: a per-period
     separates_extremes predicate (bottom bucket's max factor < top bucket's min factor); spread is
     Some only when it holds, else None; turnover is Some only when BOTH endpoints separate. The
     types changed: FactorReturns.spread_per_period and TurnoverAnalysis.top/bottom_turnover are now
     Vec<(u64, Option<f64>)>; aggregates fold over DEFINED values. Regression:
     tie_at_cutoff_withholds_spread_even_when_ic_is_defined (L1) +
     constant_factor_withholds_spread_and_turnover (integration + L7 behavioral).
  Contract locked the fixes: factor_analysis_contract gained nan_guard.quantile_mean_guard_token, a
  separation block (predicate + spread gate), and spread/turnover Option tokens; factor_analysis_check
  grew an 18th static collector (check_separation) + the per-quantile finiteness assertion, each with
  L3 + L7 non-vacuity mutation tests. Module doc "Undefined vs fabricated" updated to match.
  Re-verified: cargo test -p atp-factor-pipeline 22 L1 + 8 integration green; fmt/clippy clean;
  factor_analysis_check --require-cargo PASS (18 static); architecture_check exit 0; pytest 1712
  passed / 4 skips (L3 now 36 cases, L7 13); ruff clean. Deterministic critic APPROVE on the fix diff.
  LESSON for the SDK-boundary checklist: my pre-commit fresh-context fallback APPROVED, but the REAL
  Codex pass caught two genuine in-scope gaps the fallback (and the deterministic critic, and my own
  pre-check) missed — both were places the code violated doctrines it CLAIMED in its own docs
  (fail-closed finiteness; undefined-not-fabricated). When the contract asserts "every computed value
  is finite" or "undefined is None", grep that the GUARD actually covers EVERY producer site (here:
  the per-bucket means and the spread), not just the headline aggregates. Prefer the real Codex pass
  over the fallback before declaring a numeric feature done.

POST-REVIEW HARDENING — ROUND 2 (the user re-ran /codex:adversarial-review --base 860df19 AFTER the
round-1 fix; the re-scoped pass found TWO MORE high findings, both valid, both downstream of the
same design choice — the panel permits a DIFFERENT security set each period — both fixed in a second
fix commit on top):
  R2-A [high] "Turnover ignores removals when quantile sizes shrink": membership_turnover was the
     one-sided alphalens convention 1 - |current ∩ prior|/|current| (fraction of NEW names), which
     silently assumes a stable universe. When the current quantile is a strict SUBSET of the prior
     (the universe shrank), retained == current.len() -> turnover 0, hiding the removed names and
     understating transaction-cost drag. FIX: SYMMETRIC churn |current △ prior|/(|current|+|prior|)
     (entered + exited names). It is in [0,1], counts removals, and PROVABLY equals the one-sided
     value when the two quantiles are the same size (2k/2n == k/n) — so every existing equal-size
     turnover test stays green; only a changing universe diverges. Regression:
     shrinking_universe_turnover_counts_removals (L1) +
     turnover_counts_removals_when_the_universe_shrinks (integration + L7 behavioral).
  R2-B [high] "Cumulative spread compounds across undefined periods": cumulative_spread filtered out
     the None spreads and compounded the rest, so Some(0.1), None, Some(0.1) reported 21% — implicitly
     holding the long-short portfolio continuously THROUGH the unranked middle period (fabricated
     continuity). FIX: cumulative_spread is None unless EVERY analyzed period has a defined spread
     (path-dependent compounding requires a contiguous series). mean_spread — an average statistic,
     not a path — legitimately stays over the defined periods. Regression:
     cumulative_spread_withheld_across_an_undefined_period (L1 + integration + L7 behavioral).
  Contract locked the fixes: factor_returns gained cumulative_gate_token (any_spread_undefined),
  turnover gained symmetric_token (entered + exited); check_factor_returns / check_turnover assert
  them, each with L3 + L7 non-vacuity mutation tests. Struct docs updated (the turnover churn formula
  is now the symmetric one; cumulative_spread doc states the no-gap requirement).
  Re-verified: cargo test 24 L1 + 10 integration green; fmt/clippy clean; factor_analysis_check
  --require-cargo PASS (18 static); architecture_check exit 0; pytest 1718 passed / 4 skips (L3 39,
  L7 17); ruff clean. Deterministic critic APPROVE on the R2 diff.
  LESSON (extends the section-16 numeric-compute checklist): once a numeric series can be Option
  (undefined per period), AUDIT EVERY consumer of that series for two failure modes — (a) a
  path-dependent reduction (compounding) that must NOT silently skip the gaps, and (b) a
  cardinality-sensitive denominator (turnover, weights) that breaks when the universe size varies
  between periods. The real Codex pass found BOTH on the SECOND run, AFTER the first round already
  introduced the Option — i.e. fixing one undefined-handling bug can surface the next; re-run the
  adversarial pass after each fix round on a numeric feature, don't assume one round converges.

POST-REVIEW HARDENING — ROUND 3 (a THIRD /codex:adversarial-review --base 860df19 found TWO MORE
high findings — both deepenings of earlier rounds' fixes to their canonical correct form; fixed in
a third fix commit; 6 high findings total across 3 passes):
  R3-A [high] "Tie gate misses actual quantile cutoffs": separates_extremes only checked
     bottom_max < top_min (extreme-to-extreme). Correct for Q=2 (the lone cutoff) but for Q>=3 a tie
     can straddle the q0|q1 or q(Q-2)|q(Q-1) BOUNDING cutoff — deciding the bottom/top COMPOSITION by
     SecurityKey — while the extremes stay apart, so the spread was still fabricated. FIX: require
     BOTH bounding cutoffs untied (bottom_max < q1_min && q(Q-2)_max < top_min); captured 4 boundary
     factors in the bucket loop. Reduces to the old check at Q=2. Regression:
     inner_cutoff_tie_withholds_spread_with_three_quantiles + clean_three_quantile_factor_reports_spread
     (L1 + integration + L7). This is round-1 finding #2 completed for Q>=3.
  R3-B [high] "Changing-universe turnover understates rebalancing": the round-2 SYMMETRIC set ratio
     |cur △ prev|/(|cur|+|prev|) still ignored the WEIGHT change of RETAINED names — shrinking an
     equal-weight bucket 4->2 trades 50% of the book but the set ratio reported 33%. FIX: turnover =
     half the L1 distance between the equal-weight quantile portfolios (the standard portfolio-
     turnover / total-variation distance), = 0.5*(shared*|1/c-1/p| + entered/c + exited/p). Reduces to
     the set ratio (and the one-sided value) at equal size, so all equal-size tests stay green; the
     4->2 case is now 0.5. DETERMINISM SUBTLETY I caught (Codex did not flag it): the naive impl sums
     floats over HashSet iteration, whose order depends on the per-process random hash seed → would
     vary run-to-run and break SRS-BT-010, yet an IN-PROCESS determinism test (one seed) would NOT
     catch it. Implemented as the CLOSED FORM over integer COUNTS (filter().count() is exact, fixed
     3-term sum) so it is deterministic. Regression:
     shrinking_universe_turnover_counts_removals_and_reweighting (L1) +
     turnover_counts_removals_when_the_universe_shrinks (integration + L7).
  Contract locked the fixes: separation gained inner_cutoff_token (top_cutoff_clean); turnover's
  symmetric_token became weight_turnover_token (current_weight - previous_weight); check_separation /
  check_turnover assert them with L3 + L7 non-vacuity mutation tests. Struct/fn docs updated.
  Re-verified: cargo test 26 L1 + 11 integration green; fmt/clippy clean; factor_analysis_check
  --require-cargo PASS (18 static); architecture_check exit 0; pytest 1720 passed / 4 skips; ruff
  clean. Deterministic critic APPROVE on the R3 diff.
  LESSON (extends section-16): two cross-cutting traps on numeric features the in-process tests miss —
  (1) ANY float reduction over a HashSet/HashMap iteration is NON-deterministic across runs (random
  hash seed) even though it looks order-independent and passes a same-process determinism test; use a
  count/closed-form or sort first. (2) A "separation/boundary" predicate that's correct at the binary
  (2-bucket) case is often INSUFFICIENT at N buckets — re-derive it for the general N, don't assume the
  2-case generalizes. And the meta-lesson stands: numeric features took THREE adversarial rounds to
  converge; budget for iterate-and-reverify, and run the REAL Codex pass (not the fallback) each round.

POST-REVIEW HARDENING — ROUND 4 = SCOPE-HONEST DESCOPE (the STOP). A FOURTH
/codex:adversarial-review --base 860df19 found TWO more high findings, but BOTH had crossed the
deferred-scope boundary: they asked for portfolio-return MODELING the minimal panel deliberately does
not carry, which belongs to the deferred producer / backtest layer — NOT more analysis-surface code.
This is the SRS-BT-009 "user-ratified-deferral STOP" lesson applied: I surfaced the scope decision via
AskUserQuestion (descope+redoc / build-richer-model / accept+document) and the user chose DESCOPE+REDOC.
  R4-A [high] "Cumulative spread compounds potentially OVERLAPPING forward windows": FactorPeriod has a
     start ts only, no forward-return HORIZON, so a daily panel of 5-day forwards would compound
     overlapping windows and fabricate cumulative performance — and this surface cannot validate
     non-overlap. RESOLUTION (descope): REMOVED the cumulative_spread field + its compute entirely.
     The honest horizon-agnostic primitives stay — the per-period spread series + mean_spread (an
     average, not a compounded path). The validated compounded series is deferred to a horizon-aware
     panel (SRS-DATA-007 / SRS-FAC-001 producer that knows each forward window).
  R4-B [high] "Turnover ignores return-driven weight DRIFT of retained names": even with unchanged
     membership, a real equal-weight book drifts as each name earns a different return, and rebalancing
     that drift is real trading the metric omits. RESOLUTION (redoc, not recompute): what I compute is
     the standard TARGET / factor-SIGNAL turnover (the trading the factor's RANKING change implies) —
     a legitimate, well-defined quantity; the drift component needs holding-period returns + a
     rebalancing convention = portfolio simulation = the deferred backtest engine. REFRAMED every doc /
     evidence string from "transaction-cost turnover" to "target-portfolio (factor-signal) turnover",
     and recorded drift turnover as a deferred owner. The weight-L1 computation is UNCHANGED (it is the
     correct target turnover); only the CLAIM was softened to stop overclaiming realized cost.
  Both descopes recorded in the module Deferred doc + factor_analysis_contract.deferred[] + the check
  _DEFERRED_OWNERS, so the partial-pass scope is loud. Net surface change: FactorReturns drops
  cumulative_spread (now per_quantile_mean + spread_per_period + mean_spread); TurnoverAnalysis
  unchanged in shape, reframed in docs.
  Re-verified: cargo test 26 L1 + 11 integration green; fmt/clippy clean; factor_analysis_check
  --require-cargo PASS (18 static); architecture_check exit 0; pytest 1719 passed / 4 skips; ruff clean.
  Deterministic critic APPROVE on the R4 diff (removing struct fields + individual test fns is NOT a
  critic violation — it only blocks whole test-FILE deletion + reason-less skips, neither present).
  LESSON (the headline process lesson, extends section-16 + the SRS-BT-009 STOP): on a numeric feature,
  distinguish two kinds of adversarial finding — (i) a DEFECT/INCOMPLETENESS WITHIN the surface (rounds
  1-3 here: false-alpha, inf-leak, inner-cutoff, weight-turnover) → FIX it; vs (ii) a request for MODELING
  THE DATA MODEL CANNOT CARRY (round 4: forward-horizon, holding-period drift) → that is a SCOPE call,
  not a defect. For (ii), do NOT reflexively expand the deterministic core into the deferred producer/
  simulation layer (it never converges — the next finding is the transaction-cost model, then the
  rebalancing convention…). Instead DESCOPE the overclaiming output (remove cumulative_spread) and REDOC
  the honest one (target- not cost-turnover), record the deferral, and STOP. The tell that you've hit
  (ii): the metric keeps getting a more sophisticated PORTFOLIO model each round (one-sided → set →
  weight-L1 → drift-adjusted → cost-model…) — that escalation is the deferred backtest engine's domain.

POST-REVIEW HARDENING — ROUND 5 (the descope held — Codex did NOT re-raise the round-4 settled axes;
a fifth pass found one WITHIN-surface defect + one of MY OWN doc-drifts from the round-4 descope, both
fixed; 10 findings total across 5 passes):
  R5-A [high] "Tied factors emit fabricated per-quantile RETURNS": I had applied undefined-not-fabricated
     to IC, spread, and turnover, but kept per_quantile_mean UNCONDITIONAL (I even documented "each is a
     real mean of whatever landed"). Codex correctly challenged that the quantile-return LADDER is the
     "does this factor sort returns?" visualization, so publishing it for a constant/cutoff-tied factor
     presents symbol-ordering noise as a factor signal — the SAME false-signal class I already fixed for
     the spread. This was a genuine missed application of my own doctrine (a DEFECT, not scope). FIX:
     generalized the cleanliness check to ALL cutoffs. bucket_period now tracks each bucket's min/max
     factor, a cutoff(k|k+1) is clean iff max(k) < min(k+1), and a bucket is CLEAN iff BOTH its bounding
     cutoffs are untied. per_quantile_mean is now Vec<Vec<Option<f64>>> — a bucket mean is Some only when
     its bucket is clean, else None (per-bucket precision: a single deep tie voids only the two adjacent
     buckets, not the whole ladder). separates_extremes is now DERIVED from the same per-bucket
     cleanliness (= bucket_clean[0] && bucket_clean[Q-1]), unifying the spread/turnover gate with the
     ladder gate. Regression: constant_factor→all-None ladder; inner_cutoff_tie→only adjacent buckets
     None, far bucket Some (L1 + integration + L7).
  R5-B [medium] "Architecture contract advertises nonexistent cumulative spread": MY OWN doc-drift — the
     round-4 descope removed the field + updated the fields list + most docs, but missed the JSON block's
     prose `description` and the factor_analysis_check.py module docstring, both of which still named the
     compounded cumulative spread. FIX: scrubbed both (now describe it as deferred), and reframed the
     turnover prose to "target turnover". Lesson: when descoping, grep the FEATURE NAME across ALL prose
     (json description blobs, module/file docstrings), not just the typed fields + the nearest doc-comment.
  Contract locked R5-A: factor_returns gained per_quantile_option_token (per_quantile_mean: Vec<Vec<
     Option<f64>>>); separation's tokens updated to the match-arm gate (true, Some(bottom), Some(top)) +
     the per-bucket-derived predicate bucket_clean[0] && bucket_clean[quantiles - 1]; check_factor_returns
     asserts the ladder Option, each with L3 + L7 non-vacuity mutation tests.
  Re-verified: cargo test 27 L1 + 11 integration green; fmt/clippy clean; factor_analysis_check
  --require-cargo PASS (18 static); architecture_check exit 0; pytest 1721 passed / 4 skips; ruff clean.
  Deterministic critic APPROVE on the R5 diff.
  LESSON (final convergence note for this feature): once an undefined-not-fabricated doctrine is
  established for SOME outputs, audit it against EVERY output of the same class — here the per-bucket
  ladder was the last unguarded one (IC/spread/turnover were already guarded). And after a DESCOPE,
  feature-name-grep ALL prose for stale claims. Round 5 found exactly these two — a missed-doctrine defect
  and a descope doc-drift — i.e. convergence (cleanup of known patterns), not new escalation; the round-4
  scope axes (forward horizon, drift turnover) stayed settled.

POST-REVIEW HARDENING — ROUND 6 (a 6th pass: one within-surface DEFECT + the round-4 horizon axis
re-raised, which caught a real overclaim in MY round-4 doc; 12 findings total across 6 passes):
  R6-A [medium] "Top turnover suppressed by unrelated bottom-quantile ties": I gated BOTH turnover
     series on `separates` (both extremes clean). But top turnover depends only on the TOP bucket and
     bottom only on the BOTTOM, so a bottom-only tie wrongly suppressed a well-defined top turnover.
     A genuine within-surface precision DEFECT → FIX. PeriodBuckets now exposes bottom_clean + top_clean
     SEPARATELY (replacing separates_extremes); compute tracks previous_top_clean/previous_bottom_clean;
     top_turnover gated on (top_clean && previous_top_clean), bottom on the bottom pair; the SPREAD still
     needs both (it's top−bottom: let separates = bottom_clean && top_clean). Regression:
     bottom_only_tie_keeps_top_turnover_defined + top_only_tie_keeps_bottom_turnover_defined (L1 +
     integration + L7).
  R6-B [high] "Aggregate means mix incomparable horizons/intervals": mean_spread averages per-period
     spreads whose MAGNITUDE scales with the forward-return horizon, and the turnover means depend on the
     rebalance interval — so averaging across a panel mixing 1-day/5-day forwards or daily/monthly
     rebalances mixes incomparable quantities. This is the round-4 horizon axis re-raised, BUT it caught a
     real overclaim: my round-4 doc literally called mean_spread "horizon-agnostic", which is FALSE.
     RESOLUTION (user-chosen: document precondition + fix the claim, NOT expand the model): corrected the
     wrong claim and documented that mean_spread + turnover means assume a REGULAR panel (consistent
     forward-return horizon + rebalance interval) — the producer's contract, which this surface cannot
     validate (the panel has a start ts only); recorded horizon/interval validation as the deferred
     producer's job (new module "Panel-regularity precondition" section + per-field docs + contract). KEY
     correctness note that bounded this: the IC family (mean/std/IR) IS genuinely horizon-agnostic — it's
     a RANK correlation, independent of return magnitude — so it carries NO precondition; only the
     magnitude/interval-sensitive aggregates (mean_spread, mean turnover) do. The per-period series are
     all unaffected. Did NOT build horizon metadata (that's the deferred producer scope, same as the R4
     cumulative descope).

Design notes (the headline is the WRAP-don't-reinvent shape + 6-round adversarial hardening):
- The record bundles the seven artifacts the acceptance names, all of which already exist as
  producer types: BacktestRequest params, the SRS-BT-004 PerformanceMetrics, the Fill trade log,
  the EquityPoint equity curve, the SRS-BT-005 BenchmarkComparison, a CodeVersion, and a
  producer-supplied completed_at_ts. PLUS a StrategyParameters tuned-parameter set (the SYS-21
  "parameter set" query axis — distinct from the launch BacktestRequest; the only axis that tells
  two points of a parameter sweep apart). Codec mirrors the SRS-SIM-004 paper_state.rs discipline
  (MAGIC + FNV-1a checksum verified BEFORE building state, length-prefixed strings, sorted records,
  enum-tagged cost models); the new twist is exact f64 ratio round-trip via to_bits/from_bits.
  Restore is O(n log n) (decode -> validate -> dedup via HashSet -> sort ONCE -> construct), NOT
  the O(n^2) of a per-record sorted insert, and is allocation-safe on untrusted counts (no
  Vec::with_capacity from a decoded count, so a checksum-valid oversized count fails closed by
  exhausting the cursor). Money stays integer minor units; ratios are the metric-domain f64.
- DATE-RANGE AXIS (user-adjudicated): query_by_run_window (overlap with request.range — the SYS-21
  "find a 2020 backtest" axis) AND query_by_completion_window (the completed_at_ts axis). Both
  optional in RecordQuery. (My plan defaulted to completion-time only; Codex challenged it; user
  chose "support both".)
- COHERENCE (fail-closed validate_record, the trust boundary): trade-log coherence (fill symbol ==
  run symbol, within the equity-curve window, non-decreasing ts, positive price, non-zero qty,
  non-negative costs); the SRS-BT-004 metric-PRODUCER input invariants (non-empty + strictly
  increasing + strictly positive equity curve over positive starting cash; terminal-zero allowed);
  benchmark-identity coherence (metrics & comparison identify the SAME benchmark and share
  alpha/beta) + the excess_return == strategy_total - benchmark_total algebraic identity; per-metric
  DOMAIN bounds (win_rate & max_drawdown in [0,1], non-negative annualized_volatility); finiteness.
  from_result is the SAFE producer constructor: it takes the trade log + equity curve FROM the
  authoritative BacktestResult and verifies the result's data_source + range match the request, so
  a record cannot be persisted under false provenance.

Design / safety notes (the headline is the numeric boundary + the 7-round adversarial hardening):
- NUMERIC BOUNDARY: money enters in integer minor units (EquityPoint.equity_minor: i64,
  BenchmarkPoint.level_minor: i64, every Fill money field: i64); the eight metrics are
  dimensionless f64 RATIOS. Unlike paper_state, metrics.rs DOES contain f64 — that is the
  metric domain, not a money leak. The f64 work is DETERMINISTIC (SRS-BT-010): fixed
  left-to-right folds over ts-sorted series, no parallelism/RNG/clock; a non-monotonic ts
  is rejected. A metric undefined on the input is None (never a fabricated 0.0); every
  result is verified finite (NonFiniteComputation) so no NaN/inf leaks into a ranking.
- The metric formulas, each pinned by an L1 test: returns r_i = (E_i - E_{i-1})/E_{i-1}
  from a [baseline, ...marks] series; geometric annualized return; sample (ddof=1) vol;
  Sharpe/Sortino on excess returns over the per-period rf; beta = cov/var; JENSEN ALPHA on
  EXCESS returns ((mean_r - rf) - beta*(mean_b - rf)); max drawdown peak-to-trough; win
  rate = fraction of COMPLETE flat-to-flat round trips with strictly positive NET P&L.
- The pre-trade baseline (starting_equity_minor) is a REQUIRED compute arg, so the first
  period's P&L (incl. entry costs) is ALWAYS captured and never silently omitted; the
  benchmark carries its baseline as benchmark_levels[0] (len == equity_curve.len()+1). A
  TERMINAL-ZERO equity mark is a defined -100% total loss / 100% drawdown (not an abort);
  only a non-final non-positive or a negative final mark is rejected.
- WIN RATE robustness (the deepest-reviewed surface): NET of transaction costs (a
  gross-positive but net-negative trade is a loss); FRAGMENTATION-INVARIANT (a round trip
  closed in one fill or N volume-capped partial fills is the same trade — SYS-86
  comparability of backtest vs paper); canonicalized symbols (ledger parity); a single-fill
  reversal attributes its full cost to the closing round trip (no integer-floor bias);
  same-timestamp fills apply in execution (slice) order rather than being rejected; the
  trade log must fall within the equity curve's run window (TradeLogOutsideRun coherence
  guard).

Design / safety notes:
- DETERMINISM is the headline invariant: HashMap iteration order is unspecified, so
  serialize sorts strategies by StrategyId.as_str() (StrategyId is not Ord) and positions by
  canonical symbol before emitting, so the same state ALWAYS serializes byte-identically (a
  60s checkpoint of unchanged state never churns). Round-trip identity holds:
  restore(serialize(capture(book))) == book (incl. a flat fully-closed position that still
  carries realized P&L + commission). Codec is hand-rolled, NO serde / NO new dependency;
  integers are decimal lines, variable-length strings are length-prefixed so an OCC option
  symbol containing spaces (e.g. 'AAPL  240119C00190000') round-trips losslessly.
- FAIL-CLOSED + ATOMIC restore: deserialize validates the MAGIC header, then an FNV-1a
  integrity checksum over the body (verified BEFORE building any state), the schema version,
  the config bounds, mandatory shutdown persistence, and every position field invariant
  (quantity/basis biconditional + sign agreement, non-negative cost components, canonical
  non-empty symbols, no duplicate strategy/symbol, no trailing data), building the whole
  book in a local and returning it only on full success — so a corrupt/tampered/truncated
  snapshot returns Err with NO partially-restored book (never a phantom strategy/symbol).
- SYS-89 cadence is pinned, not just stored: interval default 60s (no upper ceiling — 60 is
  the default, not a max), restore deadline default 30s with a HARD 30s ceiling
  (RestoreDeadlineTooLong) so the config cannot encode an SLA slower than the requirement;
  shutdown persistence is MANDATORY (new() does not take the flag; it is always true; a
  snapshot encoding it disabled is rejected with ShutdownPersistenceRequired).
- Integer minor units throughout (i64 quantity, i128 money, u64 cadence/checksum), no f64,
  no broker/adapter/vendor dependency — persisted paper state is structurally independent of
  the IB account (SYS-84 isolation holds through persistence).

Design / safety notes:
- Average-cost accounting on a SIGNED cost_basis_minor (long > 0 = cash out, short < 0 =
  proceeds): open/add grows basis; reduce/close releases the PROPORTIONAL slice
  (cost_removed = cost_basis * |q| / |held|, truncated, REMAINDER stays in the basis);
  flip-through-zero fully closes then reopens at the fill price. Rounding policy chosen
  for EXACT BASIS CONSERVATION (full close -> cost_basis == 0, total P&L never leaks);
  the derived per-unit average_cost_minor can shift <1 minor unit on a partial close,
  pinned by a property-style test over many sequences (incl. the indivisible 32-over-3
  case). The alternative (avg-cost-stable) was rejected because it leaks the truncation
  remainder.
- apply_fill is ATOMIC (computes every prospective value into locals, commits only after
  all checked ops succeed) and fails closed BEFORE any mutation on: non-positive price,
  zero quantity, negative cost component (NegativeCost), inconsistent cash_delta
  (InconsistentCashDelta = the simulate_fill invariant -(notional) - total_cost),
  empty symbol, non-positive mark, overflow. A rejected first fill leaves NO phantom
  strategy/symbol (get_mut-or-insert-on-success, not entry().or_default()).
- The ledger tracks the FULL transaction-cost decomposition (commission + slippage +
  spread), so realized_pnl_minor - transaction_cost_paid_minor reconciles EXACTLY with
  the sum of the fills' cash_delta_minor (no charged cost disappears). Symbols are
  canonicalized (trim + upper-case, the SecurityKey policy) so AAPL/aapl/" AAPL " share
  one position. A symbol-keyed unrealized_pnl_minor(symbol, snapshot) surface on
  StrategyLedger/Book selects the position by symbol. Integer minor units, i128 checked
  math, no f64, &mut self deterministic, no broker/IB/vendor dependency.

a per-bar BarVolumeBudget caps each fill at its REMAINING volume and CONSUMES it, so
the SUM of fills against one bar cannot exceed observed volume even across orders; the
budget is BOUND to its bar (a budget/snapshot mismatch fails closed) so a stale or
oversized budget cannot overfill a thinner bar. The configurable per-strategy fill
model ships two BEHAVIOR-CHANGING deterministic variants (ImmediateOnCross fills a
touch, RequireThroughCross requires a strict cross). A FillDecision::Filled feeds
simulate_fill, so a triggered fill flows through the SAME cost family the backtest
engine uses and stays inside the engine (no IB API order call, reusing the SIM-001
no-broker-route crate-boundary guarantee). 7 typed FillModelError variants fail closed
before any fill.

+ cargo test --workspace green. cargo fmt --check clean (hand-applied the local
rustfmt's wrapping to new lines; NO whole-crate fmt per the no_whole_crate_cargo_fmt
note — pre-existing newer-rustfmt drift in atp-data/atp-execution/atp-orchestrator/

variants; 13 evidence items). architecture_check.py exit 0 surfacing the sim_fill

-m "not integration and not e2e" 1338 passed / 4 pre-existing pending-impl skips / 118

    fill AT -1) — fixed with validate_order_type + NonPositiveLimitPrice/StopPrice; (2)
    FillModelConfig was a no-op (LimitFillModel had one variant), so "configurable" was
    hollow — fixed by adding the behavior-changing RequireThroughCross variant + tests
    proving two configs differ on a touch; (3) the volume cap was per-call/stateless, so
    two orders could each fill the whole bar — fixed with the stateful per-bar
    BarVolumeBudget + evaluate_fill_against_budget (consumes the budget) + aggregate
    tests; (4) the budget was decoupled from the snapshot (BarVolumeBudget::new is
    public), so an oversized budget could overfill a thin bar — fixed by binding the
    budget to its bar (observed_bar_volume) and failing closed on a mismatch
    (BudgetSnapshotMismatch). Round 5 approved. This is exactly the value of the real

    every round, but Codex's deeper pass caught four genuine correctness gaps the

What I did (one feat commit 789bb9a, 8 files, +1475/-1):
- crates/atp-simulation/src/sim.rs (NEW): PaperSimulationEngine { cost_config:
  CostConfig } derives Default, so its default cost family is PROVABLY
  CostConfig::default() — the IDENTICAL SyRS baseline the backtest engine defaults
  to (SYS-15e). with_cost_config() is the per-strategy override ("unless explicitly
  configured otherwise") and never mutates the shared default. simulate_fill()
  computes the per-fill CostBreakdown via self.cost_config.cost_breakdown(quantity,
  price_minor, observed_spread_minor) — the IDENTICAL entry point BacktestEngine::
  run calls — and folds the total into a signed cash_delta_minor that ALWAYS
  SUBTRACTS the cost (a buy pays notional plus cost; a sell receives proceeds less
  cost), so a cost can never fabricate cash, mirroring the backtest engine exactly.
  PaperFill carries the same commission/slippage/spread-impact decomposition as the
  backtest Fill plus cash_delta_minor + an overflow-checked total_cost_minor().
  Minimal PaperLedger { cash_minor, position, commission_paid_minor } with
  apply_fill() is the SYS-84 seam (full ledger = SRS-SIM-003, deferred). SimError
  { EmptySymbol, NonPositivePrice, NegativeSpread, Overflow, Cost(CostError) } +
  From<CostError>; fails closed before any cost on each bad input. Integer minor
  units (i128 intermediates, i64::try_from -> Overflow, checked_*; never f64);
  every money var carries the _minor suffix so the critic's PRICE_FIELD_RE never
  matches. 11 in-module L1 unit tests.
- crates/atp-simulation/src/lib.rs: pub mod sim; (the shared-family re-export
  alongside pub mod cost;).

  tests — the PARITY proof. assert_same_costs() runs a backtest with a CostConfig to
  get a Fill, then calls simulate_fill with the SAME config + same (qty, price,
  spread), and asserts commission/slippage/spread-impact are EQUAL between the two
  engines (the SRS-BT-003 acceptance criterion), under the default family, an

verbatim, so by construction sim and backtest cannot diverge — the parity test

is deterministic. The PaperLedger is intentionally minimal (cash/position/
commission only) to stay atomic to BT-003; avg-cost + realized/unrealized P&L is
SRS-SIM-003's SYS-84 work.

Money/safety design notes: integer minor units everywhere; i128 intermediates;
deterministic div_round_half_up (ties up, non-negative inputs only); i64::try_from
narrowing -> CostError::Overflow. Sub-cent IB per-share rate is expressed in
"centi-minor per share" (1/100 of a cent) so commission stays exact in integers.
IB tiered clamp order is min(max(per_share, floor), cap) — the 1% cap is a hard
upper bound, so a sub-$0.35 tiny trade is capped below the floor (documented;
the cumulative monthly-volume tier ladder is deferred — needs cross-run state).
Observed-spread cost = half the spread per share (a single execution crosses half
the bid-ask from mid) — an interpretive but documented/overridable choice the
judgment critic explicitly accepted (SYS-15c does not prescribe a fraction).

  deferrals are documented. Stopped at round 4 to avoid iterative-deepening
  into the deferred runtime (see [[feedback_sdk_boundary_defensive_checklist]]).

/codex:adversarial-review round-4 (base a178016) raised one [medium]:
the round-3 fail-closed at the gate now REJECTS an unsupported option

DIAGNOSTIC-precision gap (the request is already rejected fail-closed —
safe — only the label/event is imprecise) on the ALREADY-deferred option
path, whose runtime (which would surface a misleading operator alert)
does not exist; the proper fix expands a previously-shipped feature
(MD-002) and lands naturally with the option-support features
(SRS-DATA-004 / SRS-EXE-004) + the operator-interface runtime. Recorded
in subscription_fanout_contract.deferred[] ("gate error precision").

=== SESSION 34 ADDENDUM 3 — Codex round-3 follow-up ===
Date: 2026-05-30
/codex:adversarial-review round-3 (base 14676d7) raised one [high]: the
option fail-closed was only enforced at subscribe/fan_out, while the
registry's try_acquire (the SubscriptionLineCounter the SRS-MD-002 gate
consumes) collapsed an uncanonicalizable request into the capacity
wildcard — so an option BELOW the line limit returned WithinLimit and
MarketDataSubscriptionManager::request_subscription falsely returned
SubscriptionAccepted (and at the limit misreported SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_
REACHED). Real bug I introduced in round 2.

Fixed (Codex's primary recommendation, in-scope MD-001 only — the MD-002
gate/trait are untouched): try_acquire now canonicalizes first via
`let Ok(key) = request.security_key() else { return ExceededLimit; }`, so
an uncanonicalizable request (option / empty symbol) fails closed and the
gate rejects it instead of falsely admitting. The precise
OptionContractUnsupported still surfaces at subscribe; a dedicated
gate-level validation stage stays deferred with the runtime. Added the
gate-level tests Codex asked for (lib option_request_is_rejected_at_the_
md_002_gate + integration srs_md_001_option_request_is_rejected_by_the_
md_002_gate, both routing an option through request_subscription with the
ConsolidatedSubscriptionRegistry as the counter, asserting rejection
below capacity) + L7 shell + a check_line_counter_impl guard requiring
try_acquire to canonicalize (request.security_key()) + its L3 mutation
spot-check. cargo test --workspace green (atp-market-data lib 18 +
srs_md_001 12 + err_4 5); full pytest 1058 passed / 0 failed; clippy +
rustfmt clean on my crates. SRS-MD-001 stays passes:false.

=== SESSION 34 ADDENDUM — Codex adversarial-review follow-up ===
Date: 2026-05-30
After the three SRS-MD-001 commits landed, the user ran the real

  (1) line-limit admission was not atomic with registry mutation —
      subscribe opened a new upstream line without checking line_limit;
      only the read-only try_acquire probe (MD-002 gate path) checked,
      leaving a probe-then-mutate race and letting a direct subscribe
      caller exceed the IB line cap;
  (2) dedup + fan-out keyed on a raw, uncanonicalized symbol String —

written RED against the old code, confirmed failing, then fixed):

- atp-types: new AssetClass { Equity, Option } (the SRS-SDK-003 tradable
  classes; futures/crypto are out of release scope; intentionally
  narrower than atp-adapters' instrument-catalog AssetClass, which lives
  ABOVE the dependency boundary so the core types cannot reuse it) and
  SecurityKey { symbol, asset_class } — PRIVATE fields, normalizing
  constructor SecurityKey::new(symbol, asset_class) that trims +
  upper-cases the symbol and returns None on empty, so a key can only be
  built canonical. asset_class added to SubscriptionRequest (MD-002's
  type) + MarketDataTick; both expose .security_key() -> Option<SecurityKey>.

- atp-market-data: ConsolidatedSubscriptionRegistry now keys the
  consolidated set on BTreeMap<SecurityKey, Vec<StrategyId>>. subscribe
  enforces the line ceiling ATOMICALLY in the same &mut borrow that
  inserts (checks `self.subscribers.len() as u32 >= self.line_limit`
  BEFORE insert, returns the new SubscriptionRegistryError::LineLimitReached
  { configured_limit } without registering anything) — closing the
  probe-then-mutate race. subscribe/unsubscribe/fan_out/subscriber_count/
  is_subscribed/try_acquire all canonicalize via SecurityKey;
  subscriber_count/is_subscribed/unsubscribe now take &SecurityKey.

- The MD-002 gate (request_subscription) is unchanged: it still consumes
  the registry as SubscriptionLineCounter (try_acquire now builds the key
  from the request). subscription_limit_contract is untouched — it only
  requires strategy_id+symbol, and asset_class is additive/non-forbidden,

- Contract (subscription_fanout_contract): added asset_class_enum,
  security_key, registry.key_type/key_field_decl, registry_error_enum
  += LineLimitReached, an atomic_admission block, and rewrote validation
  for the security_key() fail-closed path. Check script grew from 10 to

Feature completed: SRS-MD-001 SDK-SURFACE — consolidated market-data
subscription dedup + fan-out for the "consolidate duplicate real-time
market data subscriptions across active strategies" requirement per
docs/SRS.md row SRS-MD-001 (traces SyRS SYS-70; StRS SN-1.10, SN-1.29,

the SRS-MD-001 invariant — exactly ONE upstream IB subscription per
distinct security regardless of how many strategy containers subscribe;
fan_out routes a received MarketDataTick to every subscriber of its
symbol and to NO other subscriber. It publishes a SubscriptionChange-
Event (the SyRS SYS-61 / SRS-LOG-001 subscription_change event for
Source.MARKET_DATA) on every line-affecting / dedup transition through a
SubscriptionChangeSink port, fails closed (SubscriptionRegistryError)
on empty symbol / strategy id, and — the cross-feature seam — IS the
concrete SubscriptionLineCounter the SRS-MD-002 gate consumes, closing
subscription_limit_contract.deferred[]'s "owner: SRS-MD-001" item
(try_acquire is dedup-aware: a duplicate of an already-subscribed
security consumes no new line). New shared types live in
crates/atp-types (MarketDataTick, SubscriptionChange,
SubscriptionChangeEvent). The contract is pinned in
architecture/runtime_services.json#subscription_fanout_contract and

collectors + cargo smoke) + tests/test_subscription_fanout_contract.py

runner over crates/atp-market-data/tests/srs_md_001_subscription_fanout.rs.

  * the SRS AC + SyRS SYS-61 verbatim enumerate the 5 severity
    levels, 8 system-log emitter sources, and 17 event types per
    source — all AC-pinnable;
  * no python/atp_logging/ existed yet — clean slate for the SDK
    surface.

  because AsyncAPI keys are url-shaped: /ws/v1/account_status,

package — ReadinessGate state machine with discrete INITIALIZING /
PRE_TRADE_BLOCKED / READY / OVERRIDDEN states, 9 allowed + 7
forbidden transitions partitioning the full 4x4 state square; an
OperatorOverride dataclass with the four SRS-MD-006 audit-trail
fields (actor / reason / audit_trail_id / timestamp_ns) enforced at
the gate boundary; a ReadinessGateError family (PreTradeHoldError,
GateTransitionError, OverrideAuditError) so callers can catch the
hold + structural rejections with one except clause; and structured
payload renderers (as_log_records, as_dashboard_payload) that pin
the field shape for the future SRS-LOG-001 / SRS-UI-001 / SRS-API-001
consumers. The cross-language contract is pinned in
architecture/runtime_services.json#startup_readiness_gate_contract
and enforced by tools/startup_readiness_gate_check.py (25 evidence
collectors) + tests/test_startup_readiness_gate_contract.py L3
mutation suite + tests/domain/test_startup_readiness_gate.py L7
reference-boot-orchestrator end-to-end runner.

per the SDK-surface partial-pass pattern; see "What I tested" for

  reflects how many ways an "anti-internals" rule can be

  constants across all scanners instead of duplicating; (b)

  named guard, also check the alias form of `from <pkg>
  import <name>`; (d) when extracting code from docstrings,
  preserve original indentation on continuation lines; (e)
  fail closed on SyntaxError so broken examples surface
  rather than being silently skipped; (f) tighten markdown
  fence regex to require explicit language tags so prose
  between fences cannot be mistaken for code.

Feature completed: SRS-SDK-006 — built-in technical indicator
library wrapping pandas-ta + TA-Lib per SyRS SYS-35 / AC-6 / StRS
SN-1.20 / C-9. The SDK ships SMA / EMA / RSI / MACD / BollingerBands /

wrappers — buffering, dtype conversion, and NaN -> None glue only,
no arithmetic — over both reference libraries. SMA + BollingerBands
route through pandas_ta; EMA / RSI / MACD / ATR route through TA-Lib.

both" requirement is satisfied end-to-end, not just at the import
line. Numerical parity is pinned against the OTHER library too via
the L7 + L2 + evidence-script paths. Public surface stays byte-
compatible with the prior pure-Python placeholder so existing call
sites (tests/test_strategy_api.py, tests/domain/test_warmup_replay.py,

Feature completed: SRS-SDK-005 — Python Strategy API warm-up
mechanism. The SDK ships a WarmupController + WarmupState
lifecycle + assert_warmup_complete guard that future
dispatchers (live SRS-EXE-001, paper SRS-SIM-001, backtest
SRS-BT-001) drive before the first executable bar; the L7
reference dispatcher exercises the AC end-to-end with a 200-
bar replay + SMA(200) ready-at-boundary check. Unlike
SRS-SDK-004 (which deferred for NFR-P4 latency proof), SDK-005
has no NFR latency gate — its AC is purely behavioural ordering
+ indicator buffer state, fully provable at the SDK surface.
Status: 94 remaining features (was 95 at start of session).

What I did:
- Carryover audit at session start: SESSION 27's "Lowest
  remaining P1 by ID in the SRS-SDK chain is SRS-SDK-005" was
  sound. ERR-7 / ERR-8 / ERR-9 / SRS-API-001 / SRS-BT-* /
  SRS-DATA-* / SRS-RESV-* / SRS-SAFE-* / SRS-EXE-* / SRS-SIM-* /
  SRS-MD-* remain blocked on subsystems not yet built.

- Prep commit (cae811f): extended SAFETY_PATH_RE in
  tools/critic_check.py to add `strategy[_-]?api[_-]?warmup`,
  `warm[_-]?up[_-]?replay`, `warmup[_-]?controller`,
  `warmup[_-]?state`, `warmup[_-]?bars`,
  `indicator[_-]?initialization`, `historical[_-]?replay`
  tokens. Mirrors the SESSION 16-27 per-feature prep precedent.

- Feat commit (76c0f00, +1786 / -5, 10 files): shipped the
  warm-up SDK surface. New python/atp_strategy/warmup.py
  exposes WarmupState (PENDING / IN_PROGRESS / COMPLETE),
  WarmupController (state / warmup_bars / bars_replayed /
  symbols_replayed properties, run() method), and
  assert_warmup_complete(state) guard. The controller pulls
  warmup_bars historical bars per subscribed symbol, replays
  them through Strategy.on_bar in order, transitions to
  COMPLETE, then fires on_warmup_complete exactly once.

  Critical safety property the first /codex:adversarial-review
  pass surfaced (and the second pass approved after the fix):
  the controller is fail-closed on a short historical replay.
  If HistoricalData.get_bars returns fewer than warmup_bars
  bars for any subscribed symbol the controller raises
  WarmupNotComplete with a "short by N bars" message, leaves
  WarmupState at IN_PROGRESS, does NOT fire on_warmup_complete,
  and keeps assert_warmup_complete closed. Production
  dispatchers must halt the container and surface the failure
  to the operator rather than enter live trading with an
  unready indicator (a 200-period SMA needs at least 200 bars
  to become ready).

  Architecture metadata block strategy_api_warmup_contract is
  the cross-language source of truth: state members, canonical
  200-bar warm-up, helper functions, exports, docstring tokens,
  AC traces, deferred dispatcher ownership, and the explicit
  fail-closed history-shortfall behaviour Rust core dispatchers
  re-implement locally per AGENTS.md dependency direction (no
  Rust -> Python SDK dependency).

  Contract evidence script tools/strategy_api_warmup_check.py
  + wiring in tools/architecture_check.py + init.sh.

  L7 domain test tests/domain/test_warmup_replay.py: reference
  _RefDispatcher exercises the AC end-to-end with 200 historical
  bars + SMA(200), executable-bar / order-submission gating
  during warm-up, on_warmup_complete fires-exactly-once at the
  boundary, live/paper parity (same surface), NFR-R3 restart
  re-execution, short-history fail-closed cases (single + multi-
  subscription), and the zero-warmup degenerate path. 13 tests.

  L3 contract tests/test_strategy_api_warmup_contract.py:
  subprocess positive-evidence check + mutation rig that locks
  WarmupState members, controller method/property shape, the
  on_warmup_complete signature + docstring tokens, the short-
  history shortfall guard, the assert_warmup_complete body, and
  the package-level exports. 15 tests.

- This SESSION 28 chore commit: appends this entry to
  progress.txt and flips SRS-SDK-005 passes:true in
  feature_list.json.

=== SESSION 27 ===
Date: 2026-05-19
Feature completed: NONE — SDK-surface for SRS-SDK-004 shipped as
prep, SRS-SDK-004 stays passes:false. Per /codex:adversarial-review
the NFR-P4 latency-proof half of the AC (live <1000 ms p95 from
broker fill acknowledgement; paper <100 ms p95 from simulated fill)
requires SRS-EXE-001 (live IB execution) and SRS-SIM-001 (internal
paper simulation) which are not yet built. Marking passes:true on
the SDK surface alone would let CI green-light a feature whose
performance gate is not actually verified. Per
[[feedback-scope-honesty]] the honest move is to surface the
finding and defer: the SDK surface is real value (future
dispatchers will satisfy this contract), but the feature stays
failing until its end-to-end AC can be proven.
Status: 95 remaining features (unchanged from SESSION 26).

  tools/critic_check.py to add `strategy[_-]?api[_-]?order[_-]?events`,
  `order[_-]?event[_-]?payload`, and `callback[_-]?latency` tokens.

- Feat commit (f4c34e1, +3413 / -9, 11 files): shipped the SDK
  boundary that the future live (SRS-EXE-001) and paper
  (SRS-SIM-001) dispatchers will satisfy. After 9 rounds of
  /codex:adversarial-review iterative deepening, the boundary
  enforces (1) payload-shape (rejects None, dict, schema-drifted
  payloads with a structured error), (2) event-type discriminant
  (rejects bare-string / unknown / non-enum event_type), (3)
  runtime type + finite validation (str identifiers; finite int/
  float fill_price + commission; non-negative int fill_quantity +
  cumulative_filled + remaining_quantity), (4) AC-named-four
  field-presence (FILL/PARTIAL_FILL/CANCELLED/REJECTED must carry
  fill_price/fill_quantity/commission), (5) sign discipline
  (fill_price never negative; FILL/PARTIAL_FILL require strictly
  positive fill_price + fill_quantity), (6) lifecycle consistency
  (FILL.remaining_quantity == 0; PARTIAL_FILL.remaining_quantity
  > 0; CANCELLED/REJECTED.fill_quantity == cumulative_filled), (7)
  terminal reason on CANCELLED/REJECTED/EXPIRED. Latency budgets
  exposed as LIVE_/PAPER_CALLBACK_LATENCY_P95_MS — the Python-
  side view of the cross-language source of truth in
  architecture/runtime_services.json (Rust core dispatchers read
  the metadata directly per AGENTS.md dependency direction; the
  contract check enforces parity).

  explicitly so the Rust implementation has a single source of
  truth to consult.

=== SESSION 26 ===
Date: 2026-05-18
Feature completed: SRS-SDK-003 — enforce single tradable asset class
invariant. The Python Strategy SDK now ships a public
``assert_asset_class(config, request)`` helper (raises
``AssetClassViolation`` when ``request.asset_class !=
config.tradable_asset_class``, with a message naming the strategy_id
and offending class for the SyRS SYS-64 structured-error contract).
``StrategyContext.order``'s Protocol docstring publicly commits to
the guard so live IB execution and internal paper simulation
drivers re-use the shipped helper rather than reimplementing the
comparison (AC-14 parity). Subscriptions remain ungated:
``StrategyContext.subscribe(symbol, asset_class=AssetClass.EQUITY)``
accepts either ``EQUITY`` or ``OPTION`` for both tradable classes per
SRS-SDK-003 AC half-A.
Status: 95 remaining features

- L3 mutation rig sys.modules side effect: any future L1 test
  that does a fresh ``import atp_strategy`` inside a test body
  (not at module level) will silently get the last L3 tmpdir's
  mutated module after teardown. The contract-check tool's
  ``_load_sdk_module`` does not restore sys.modules on close.
  Two safe patterns: (a) module-level imports only in L1 tests
  (current convention; both test_scheduler.py and the new
  test_asset_class_guard.py follow this); (b) harden
  ``_load_sdk_module`` and the L3 _MutationRig to track and
  restore the original sys.modules['atp_strategy'] entry on
  close. (a) is the established repo convention; (b) is a
  defensive hardening that could ship alongside whatever feature
  next touches the scheduler or subscriptions check tools.

Date: 2026-05-18
Feature completed: SRS-SDK-002 — trading-calendar-aware scheduling
primitives. The Python Strategy SDK now ships real NYSE / NASDAQ /
CBOE-aliased calendar resolution backed by exchange_calendars: NYSE
2026 holidays and early closes, DST spring-forward (2026-03-08) and
fall-back (2026-11-01) wall-clock preservation, 04:00–20:00 ET pre-
market and after-hours session boundaries, and a concrete
InMemoryScheduler resolving the four Scheduler Protocol methods
(at_market_open, at_market_close, every_n_minutes, cron) against the
calendar. Calendar horizon pinned to [2000-01-01, 2035-12-31] for
date-deterministic resolution; cron preserves wall-clock across DST
by localizing via pytz internally; cron registration uses a fixed
sentinel (no host-clock read); every_n_minutes snaps post-close
candidates to the next session open; offset and cron candidates are
validated against the [04:00, 20:00] ET window; cross-scheduler
handles are rejected by scheduler-identity check. NotATradingSession
and CalendarHorizonExceeded surface programming errors / stale-data
conditions cleanly. SyRS AC: SYS-6 + SYS-50 + SYS-51.
Status: 96 remaining features

    Protocol methods. _CronAdapter wraps croniter — localizes base via
    pytz so wall-clock time is preserved across DST (zoneinfo + croniter
    drifts), then converts results back to zoneinfo on return. cron()
    validates syntax against a fixed sentinel `2000-01-01T12:00`
    (no datetime.now() — deterministic-time rule). next_fire_time
    rejects cross-scheduler handles by checking handle.scheduler is
    self. _resolve_market_open/close validate offset-derived fire is
    inside [premarket_open, afterhours_close] of the same session.
    _resolve_every_n snaps post-close candidates to next session open.
    _resolve_cron walks until elapsed-time deadline
    (_CRON_LOOKAHEAD_DAYS = 380; covers monthly crons with leap-year
    slack; yearly crons explicitly out of scope). All paths catch the
    lib's CalendarHorizonExceeded and convert to clear ValueError.

Override (CBOE alias):
- exchange_calendars ships no dedicated CBOE Options calendar
  (XCBO unavailable; XCBF is CBOE Futures with 16:15 ET close + Chicago
  tz — wrong asset class). NYSE / NASDAQ / CBOE-Options share the SIFMA
  U.S.-equity-class regular-session holiday calendar in practice for
  2026; the alias is correct for the strategy SDK's equity-class option
  workflows. CBOE-specific option-only early closes are deferred.
  Locked by CboeAliasDocumentedOverrideTest which asserts both the
  _EXCHANGE_HANDLES["CBOE"] = "XNYS" mapping AND the deferred[] string
  mentioning the alias rationale, so any silent regression trips the
  test. _EXCHANGE_HANDLES is the single point of update if a real
  handle lands. Owner: future feature shipping maintained CBOE Options
  session tables.

deployed code version (source hash + deployment timestamp) for each
strategy at deployment time and exposes it through a queryable
DeployedVersionRegistry port. SyRS SYS-79 wire form pinned at
`sha256:<64-hex>`; misformed hashes refused with
DEPLOYED_VERSION_INVALID before runtime.create; DeadlineExceeded
launches skip the version record (a version that was never deployed
must not appear in the active-strategy inventory or REST API
listing); deferred dashboard (SYS-41), REST API (IF-9), and backtest
result rows (SYS-21) will render the same canonical
version_identifier produced by DeployedVersion::version_identifier.

- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `OrderErrorCategory::DeployedVersionInvalid` variant with
    wire string `"DEPLOYED_VERSION_INVALID"`.
  * Added 3 spec-literal / validation-bound constants
    (SOURCE_HASH_ALGORITHM_PREFIX = "sha256:",
    SOURCE_HASH_DIGEST_HEX_LENGTH = 64, SOURCE_HASH_TOTAL_LENGTH = 71).
  * Added `SourceHash(String)` newtype with new() (infallible,
    matches ResourceProfile pattern — validation is at-boundary so
    test fixtures + env-var parsers can build the value the same
    way the gate does), validate() / validate_str() / as_str() /
    algorithm() / digest(). Validation enforces the `sha256:`
    prefix, the 64-hex-char length, AND rejects upper-case hex
    (the wire form is lower-case so round-trips are stable).
  * Added `SourceHashError` enum (4 variants): MissingAlgorithmPrefix,
    UnknownAlgorithm{found}, InvalidDigestLength{found, expected},
    NonHexDigest{found}.
  * Added `DeployedVersion { source_hash, deployed_at_seconds }`
    with new() / version_identifier(). The canonical form is
    `"<hash>@<timestamp>"` (the `@` separator avoids collision
    with the algorithm-prefix `:` and the hex alphabet) — single
    source of truth for the SYS-79 "same version identifier"
    guarantee. Forbidden-fields list (8 tokens) rejects
    docker_image / container_id / vendor / host_path / git_commit
    / git_branch / build_number / ci_run_id (coupling the audit
    shape to a build-system artifact would force multiple
    identifiers per code version, breaking the single-identifier
    guarantee).
  * Changed `StrategyLaunchRequest.deployment_hash: String →
    SourceHash` so the typed wrapper marks intent and the gate can
    validate at the orchestrator boundary.
  * Added `StrategyLaunchOutcome.deployed_version: DeployedVersion`
    (5 → 6 fields) carrying the recorded version to callers.
  * Added `StructuredOrchestratorError::deployed_version_invalid(
    request, violation)` factory mirroring the
    `resource_profile_invalid` pattern, with the category invariant
    pinned via `debug_assert!`.
  * Updated the enclosing struct Rustdoc to name all four
    orchestrator-rejection categories.
  * 12 new in-crate unit tests covering: the spec constants, the
    SourceHash validate happy path + 6 rejection variants
    (missing prefix, unknown algorithm md5, short digest, long
    digest, non-hex digest, upper-case hex), DeployedVersion
    exhaustive destructure, version_identifier canonical-form
    pin, deployed_version_invalid factory + wire-string pin,
    OrderErrorCategory wire string.
- Extended `crates/atp-orchestrator/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added new port `DeployedVersionRegistry`:
      - `fn record(&self, strategy_id: &StrategyId, version:
        DeployedVersion) -> Result<(), DeployedVersionRegistryError>`
      - `fn lookup(&self, strategy_id: &StrategyId) ->
        Result<Option<DeployedVersion>, DeployedVersionRegistryError>`
    Both methods return Result so concrete adapters (durable-store
    outage, permission denied, registry desync) surface failures
    through the typed `DeployedVersionRegistryError`. Forbidden-
    imports list (sha2 / sha1 / md5 / blake3 / sled / rusqlite /
    redis / git2) keeps the orchestrator crate clean — concrete
    registry + hash-compute adapters live in separate crates that
    haven't shipped yet.
  * Added `DeployedVersionRegistryError { reason: String }` typed
    error struct with Display + std::error::Error.
  * Extended `launch()` with a 5th parameter `version_registry: &V`:
      1. Validate `request.deployment_hash.validate()` BEFORE
         `runtime.create` (defence in depth — rejection through
         `deployed_version_invalid(...)` with NO sink event, NO
         runtime mutation; no container exists to destroy).
      2. After resource-profile validation: `runtime.create` +
         `runtime.start`.
      3. On `ReadyWithinDeadline`: build `DeployedVersion::new(
         request.deployment_hash.clone(), observed_at_seconds)` and
         call `version_registry.record(...)`. Record failures are
         best-effort (matches WorkloadEventSink pattern) — the
         typed surface exists for concrete sinks and wrapping
         callers to observe.
      4. On `DeadlineExceeded`: skip the record (a version that
         was never deployed must not appear in the active-
         strategy inventory or REST API listing).
  * Added `deployed_version_for(request, observed_at_seconds)`
    helper that produces the same record the gate would build —
    callers can preview the version identifier without invoking
    the runtime port.
  * 5 new in-crate orchestrator tests covering: happy-path
    recording + outcome equality, DeadlineExceeded skipping
    record (ForbiddenVersionRegistry panics if touched),
    malformed-hash rejection without runtime invocation,
    record-failure-does-not-abort-launch (FlakyRegistry returning
    Err), helper-produces-same-record-as-launch.

enforces the SyRS SYS-57 workload-priority hierarchy against the
configured host memory safety margin (default 2048 MB; catalogue
floor/ceiling 256..1048576 MB). New workloads refused when the
post-admit host memory would dip below the margin; the lowest-priority
active *batch* workload is evicted when a higher-priority workload
arrives; live strategy execution is never selected for eviction
(SYS-58 last clause).
Status: 99 remaining features

What I did:
- Carryover audit at session start: SRS-ORCH-003 is the next P1 by
  the autonomous-prompt's "lowest ID at the top priority tier" rule
  (SESSION 21 named it as the natural next after SRS-ORCH-002).
  Both deferred-item lists in `architecture/runtime_services.json`
  explicitly named SRS-ORCH-003 as the owner of the workload-priority
  arbitration gate, so the foundation (StrategyOrchestrator, launch,
  ResourceProfile, StructuredOrchestratorError, HealthCheckEventSink)
  was already in place.

- Prep commit (764bd76): extended SAFETY_PATH_RE in
  `tools/critic_check.py` to add the `workload[_-]?priority` and
  `host[_-]?memory[_-]?safety` tokens. Mirrors the SESSION 16-21
  prep precedent (c488029 / 7064c49 / 24391a0 / ff10ef0 / 8143ac5).

- Feat commit (bbf9f4e):
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `OrderErrorCategory::HostMemorySafetyMarginBreach` variant
    with wire string `"HOST_MEMORY_SAFETY_MARGIN_BREACH"`.
  * Added 3 spec-literal / validation-bound constants
    (HOST_MEMORY_SAFETY_MARGIN_MB_DEFAULT = 2048,
    _FLOOR = 256, _CEILING = 1_048_576).
  * Added `HostMemorySafetyMargin { mb: u32 }` with new() /
    default_margin() / validate() and `HostMemorySafetyMarginError`
    (BelowFloor / AboveCeiling).
  * Added `WorkloadPriority` enum (7 SYS-57 variants:
    LiveStrategy=1, MarketDataSubscriptionManager=2,
    PaperStrategy=3, NightlyDataIngestion=4, FactorPipeline=5,
    Backtest=6, Research=7) with rank() projection and
    `default_kind()` mapping. Forbidden-tokens list locks
    priority_score / priority_weight / priority_quota /
    priority_class_id out so the enum stays categorical.
  * Added `WorkloadKind` enum (Continuous, Batch) with is_batch()
    and `WorkloadId(String)` newtype.
  * Added `RegisteredWorkload { id, priority, kind, profile }` (4
    fields; forbidden-fields list rejects docker_image, vendor,
    container_id, host_path, broker, started_at, uptime_seconds).
  * Added `WorkloadAdmissionReason::HostMemoryBelowSafetyMargin
    { available_mb, safety_margin_mb }`.
  * Added `WorkloadAdmissionEvent` with 5 variants — Refused,
    Terminated, TerminationFailed (Docker / cgroup termination
    failure surfaced explicitly), HostProbeFailed (sysinfo / procfs
    probe failure), RegistryListingFailed (Docker engine timeout /
    in-process registry desync).
  * Added `StructuredOrchestratorError::host_memory_safety_margin_breach
    (request, available_mb, safety_margin_mb)` factory mirroring the
    `resource_profile_invalid` / `startup_deadline_exceeded`
    patterns. Updated the Rustdoc on the enclosing struct to name
    all three orchestrator-rejection categories.
  * 14 new in-crate unit tests covering the constants, validation
    paths, rank ordering, kind mapping, event variants, factory
    wire-string pin, and OrderErrorCategory mapping.
- Extended `crates/atp-orchestrator/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added three new ports:
      - `HostMemoryProbe { fn available_mb() -> Result<u64, HostMemoryProbeError> }`
      - `WorkloadRegistry { fn active() -> Result<Vec<RegisteredWorkload>, WorkloadRegistryError>; fn terminate(&WorkloadId) -> Result<(), WorkloadTerminationError> }`
      - `WorkloadEventSink { fn record(WorkloadAdmissionEvent) -> Result<(), WorkloadEventSinkError> }`
    Each carries a typed error surface. Forbidden-imports list
    (sysinfo / procfs / psutil / bollard / docker_api / shiplift /
    cgroups_rs) keeps the orchestrator crate clean — concrete
    adapters live in separate crates that haven't shipped yet.
  * Added 4 typed-error structs (HostMemoryProbeError,
    WorkloadRegistryError, WorkloadTerminationError {workload_id,
    reason}, WorkloadEventSinkError) with Display + std::error::Error.
  * Added `host_memory_safety_margin_default`,
    `safety_margin_from_lookup`, `safety_margin_via_env_lookup`,
    `safety_margin_from_env` (reads ATP_HOST_MEMORY_SAFETY_MARGIN_MB
    distinguishing NotPresent / NotUnicode / unparseable / out-of-range).
  * Added `admit_workload(request, workload_id, priority,
    safety_margin, host, registry, sink, observed_at_seconds)`. The
    algorithm:
      1. Validate the safety margin (defence in depth — defends
         against programmatic override below the floor).
      2. Probe host memory; on Err emit HostProbeFailed event and
         refuse with HostMemorySafetyMarginBreach.
      3. Happy path: if available - needed >= margin, admit silently
         (no events, no registry mutation).
      4. Otherwise list active workloads; on Err emit
         RegistryListingFailed event and refuse.
      5. Pre-eviction feasibility: filter to Batch ∧ rank > new's
         rank, sort lowest-priority-first, sum recoverable mem.
         If even the full sum cannot reach the margin → refuse
         WITHOUT calling terminate (prevents partial-eviction-refusal
         where work is killed and admission still denied).
      6. Eviction loop: terminate each candidate; on Ok emit
         Terminated event + bank freed memory + early-return when
         post-admit headroom satisfies the margin; on Err emit
         TerminationFailed event with the typed reason and continue
         to the next candidate.
      7. Post-loop refusal: emit Refused event + return breach error.
    Live-immunity debug_assert pins the SyRS SYS-58 last-clause
    invariant inside the eviction loop. The launch() Rustdoc now
    states admit_workload is a REQUIRED PRECONDITION (the typed
    coupling via AdmissionToken / typestate is deferred to the
    production-caller session).
  * 18 new in-crate orchestrator tests covering admission happy
    path, refusal with no batch evictable, eviction success,
    lowest-priority-first ordering, Continuous immunity, Live
    immunity (debug_assert), feasibility-driven refusal without
    eviction, configurable margin override, env-var helper
    (default fallback, in-range override, unparseable, below-floor,
    NotUnicode), probe-error fail-closed, registry-active-error
    fail-closed, flaky-registry partial-failure (TerminationFailed
    event with typed reason), invalid-margin + probe-failure
    routing through HostProbeFailed.

    `PAPER_PROFILE_CPU_HUNDREDTHS = 10`) and 4 catalogue-aligned

  * Added `pub struct ResourceProfile { mem_mb: u32, cpu_hundredths:
    u32 }` with `live_default()`, `paper_default()`, `for_mode()`
    (mode-keyed dispatch with exhaustive match on StrategyMode), and
    `validate()` (enforces the SRS-ARCH-005 catalogue bounds).

- Extended `crates/atp-orchestrator/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added a validation gate to `launch()` that calls
    `request.profile.validate()` BEFORE `runtime.create()` — on
    failure returns
    `StructuredOrchestratorError::resource_profile_invalid(...)` with
    NO sink event (no container exists to destroy; emitting an event
    would lie about a destroy that never happened — Pattern A,
    matches ERR-4/5/6 structured-rejection).
  * Threaded `request.profile` through the happy-path outcome:
    `StrategyLaunchOutcome { ..., profile: request.profile }`. The
    contract block enforces `profile: request.profile` literally
    appears at the construction site (no silent re-defaulting).
  * Added `live_profile_default()`, `paper_profile_default()`,
    `profile_for_mode(mode)` re-exporters on `StrategyOrchestrator`
    so callers don't have to reach into atp-types.
  * Built the env-var → launch-profile WIRE (the substantive
    enhancement the user requested): three new functions on
    `StrategyOrchestrator`:
      - `profile_for_mode_from_lookup<F: Fn(&str) -> Option<String>>`
        — pure, lookup-based; tests drive it with stub maps.
      - `profile_for_mode_via_env_lookup<F: Fn(&str) ->
        Result<String, std::env::VarError>>` — testable bridge
        that distinguishes `VarError::NotPresent` (silently falls
        back to SyRS default) from `VarError::NotUnicode` (returns
        a structured `ResourceProfileEnvError::Unparseable*` —
        a set-but-invalid override is the OPPOSITE of "configuration
        overrides are validated" so it must surface, not collapse).
      - `profile_for_mode_from_env(mode)` — production wrapper that
        plugs `std::env::var` into `_via_env_lookup`.
    Reads ATP_LIVE_STRATEGY_MEM_MB / _CPU and ATP_PAPER_STRATEGY_MEM_MB
    / _CPU; converts cores → hundredths AT THE BOUNDARY (CPU stored
    as f64 in catalogue, u32 hundredths in atp-types); validates the
    f64 cores against the f64 catalogue bounds (0.05..16.0) BEFORE
    rounding to u32 hundredths, so 0.046 cores is rejected as
    below-floor instead of silently rounding up to 5 hundredths and
    passing the integer check (symmetric for above-ceiling 16.004).
    The 1e-9 tolerance in the f64 bounds-check absorbs binary-float
    representation noise without rejecting the exact floor / ceiling.
  * Added `pub enum ResourceProfileEnvError` (UnparseableMem /
    UnparseableCpu / Validation(ResourceProfileError) variants)
    with Display + std::error::Error. The `From<ResourceProfileError>`
    impl lets the `?` operator collapse validation errors into the
    env-error envelope cleanly.
  * 14 new in-crate unit tests covering: the validation gate
    (happy-path, 4 rejection variants), the env-var wire (defaults,
    in-range overrides, unparseable mem / cpu, below-floor /
    above-ceiling, exact-floor / exact-ceiling boundary, NotPresent
    fallback, NotUnicode rejection on mem AND cpu, present-value
    threading).

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- **Concrete Docker StrategyContainerRuntime is still deferred.**
  Same shape as SESSION 20's audit conclusion: the Rust workspace
  is fully sync (zero tokio / async); a bollard-based driver implies
  a workspace-wide async refactor or a `block_on()` anti-pattern.
  No forcing function until either (a) SRS-ORCH-003 workload-priority
  arbitration lands and needs to actually destroy containers when
  the host margin is breached, or (b) a Rust orchestrator service
  binary is built that calls launch() against a real runtime
  (today main.py is still `pass` and there is no Rust binary).
- **Typed error surface on the lifecycle port is paired with the
  Docker driver.** create / stop / restart / destroy currently
  return unit. When the Docker driver lands, those signatures need
  a typed error variant (e.g.
  `Result<(), ContainerRuntimeError>` covering cgroup-creation
  failure, insufficient host resources, network failures). This is
  SRS-ORCH-001 trait-signature retrofit scope; the
  resource_profile_contract.deferred list names it.
- **Real next P1 by orchestrator-family ID order:**
  **SRS-ORCH-003** (enforce workload priority when the host memory
  safety margin would be breached). Has all the prerequisite
  infrastructure ready:
  - `ATP_HOST_MEMORY_SAFETY_MARGIN_MB` env var with default 2048,
    min 256, max 1048576 in the catalogue (SRS-ARCH-005 PASS).
  - `ResourceProfile` types and `validate()` method available from
    this session.
  - The 5 priority slots SyRS SYS-57 names — live strategy >
    market data subscription > paper strategies > nightly ingestion >
    factor pipeline > backtest > research — would need a new
    `WorkloadPriority` enum in atp-types with the same exhaustive-
    destructure invariant SRS-ORCH-001 / SRS-ORCH-002 used, plus a
    new gate function on `StrategyOrchestrator` that consults host
    memory before allowing a launch.
  - Same 3-commit cadence: prep (extend SAFETY_PATH_RE with
    `workload[_-]?priority` and `host[_-]?memory[_-]?margin`), feat
    (types + gate + contract block + check script + integration
    test + L7 domain test), chore (flip passes:true + record
    SESSION 22 progress notes).
- **SRS-ORCH-004** (deployment version surface) is the third
  orchestrator-family P1 — deployment_hash is already on
