=== SESSION 19 ===
Date: 2026-05-14
Feature completed: SRS-ORCH-001 — Strategy Orchestrator owns strategy
container lifecycle (SyRS SYS-10): launch / observe-health gates flow
exclusively through StrategyContainerRuntime + HealthCheckEventSink
ports, the NFR-P9 30-second startup budget is enforced via
LaunchReadiness, an over-deadline launch destroys the half-launched
container BEFORE recording the dashboard event (SRS-ORCH-002 / SyRS
SYS-57 resource release; ordered destroy-then-record so a sink
failure cannot mask the resource release), and an Unresponsive
container is atomically restarted AND surfaced on the dashboard
(SYS-13 selectivity: a Healthy probe is read-only). AC-12 boundary
(no strategy may manage another container) stays enforced by the
existing dependency_boundary_check `atp_orchestrator` forbidden
import already on every lower-layer crate.
Status: 101 remaining features

What I did:
- Prep commit (7064c49): extended SAFETY_PATH_RE in
  `tools/critic_check.py` to add `orchestrator[_-]?lifecycle` and
  `strategy[_-]?container` tokens. Continues the per-feature
  precedent (ERR-4 added subscription_limit + market_data_line, ERR-5
  added ingestion_validation + record_quarantine, ERR-6 added
  pacing_budget + ingestion_schedule). The L7 domain test at
  `tests/domain/test_orchestrator_lifecycle.py` and the contract
  tool at `tools/orchestrator_lifecycle_check.py` now trigger
  safety:paired-test-required if a future change touches either
  side.
- Feat commit (00389d5):
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `StrategyStartupDeadlineExceeded` variant to
    `OrderErrorCategory` (now 10 variants) with wire string
    `"STRATEGY_STARTUP_DEADLINE_EXCEEDED"` — single source of truth
    for the SyRS SYS-64 wire vocabulary; no parallel enum.
  * Added `pub const STRATEGY_STARTUP_DEADLINE_MS: u64 = 30_000` —
    the NFR-P9 30-second budget single source of truth. Future
    tuning has exactly one site.
  * Added `pub enum ContainerLifecycleAction { Create, Start, Stop,
    Restart, Destroy }` with `as_str()` map. Five variants exactly
    cover the SyRS SYS-10 lifecycle vocabulary; an exhaustive match
    would fail to compile if a variant were dropped.
  * Added `pub enum ContainerHealthState { Healthy, Unresponsive }`
    with `is_unresponsive()` helper. Two-state SYS-13 auto-restart
    trigger classifier.
  * Added `pub enum LaunchReadiness { ReadyWithinDeadline {
    elapsed_millis }, DeadlineExceeded { elapsed_millis,
    deadline_millis } }`. Struct-variant enum: the elapsed time is
    available on BOTH branches so the dashboard can render
    percentile histograms without re-probing; the deadline is
    carried on the exceeded variant for TOCTOU closure (same
    rationale as ERR-4 / ERR-6's "carry the limit on the event").
  * Added `pub struct StrategyLaunchRequest { strategy_id,
    mode: StrategyMode, deployment_hash: String, deadline_millis:
    u64 }`. Four fields, deliberately no docker_image /
    container_id / host_path / vendor / broker / ib_session_id
    (forbidden-list locked by the contract block).
  * Added `pub struct StrategyLaunchOutcome { strategy_id,
    ready_within_deadline: bool, elapsed_millis: u64,
    deadline_millis: u64 }`. Four fields, same forbidden-list.
  * Added `pub struct ContainerHealthEvent { state:
    ContainerHealthState, strategy_id, action_taken:
    ContainerLifecycleAction, observed_at_seconds: u64 }`.
    Carrying `action_taken` on the event closes a TOCTOU window —
    the dashboard can render "restarted at T" / "destroyed at T"
    without a second probe.
  * Added `pub struct StructuredOrchestratorError` with factory
    `startup_deadline_exceeded(request, elapsed_millis,
    deadline_millis)`. Reuses
    `OrderErrorCategory::StrategyStartupDeadlineExceeded` as the
    wire-string source of truth (mirrors the
    StructuredPacingError / StructuredIngestionError /
    StructuredSubscriptionError pattern).
  * Added 8 in-crate unit tests in `atp-types` covering: action
    enum exhaustiveness, health-state exhaustiveness, readiness
    enum payload shape, the NFR-P9 constant value, the
    exhaustive-destructure proof of "exactly four fields" for each
    new struct, and the factory's wire-string / message /
    Display-format invariants.
- Extended `crates/atp-orchestrator/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `trait StrategyContainerRuntime` with six methods:
    create, start (returns LaunchReadiness), stop, restart, destroy,
    health (returns ContainerHealthState). The trait lives in
    `atp-orchestrator` (NOT `atp-types`) because the consumer
    lives here; lower-layer crates cannot import
    `atp_orchestrator` (dependency_boundary_check already lists it
    as a forbidden token).
  * Added `trait HealthCheckEventSink { fn record(&self, event:
    ContainerHealthEvent); }` — the structured-event publication
    channel (dashboard WebSocket + SRS-LOG-001 audit log +
    SRS-NOTIF-001 dispatcher fan-out, all deferred to those
    features).
  * Added `pub fn launch<R, S>(&self, request:
    StrategyLaunchRequest, runtime: &R, sink: &S,
    observed_at_seconds: u64) -> Result<StrategyLaunchOutcome,
    StructuredOrchestratorError>`. Matches on
    `LaunchReadiness`; ReadyWithinDeadline returns
    `StrategyLaunchOutcome` (the ONLY construction site);
    DeadlineExceeded calls `runtime.destroy(&request.strategy_id)`
    FIRST (SRS-ORCH-002 / SyRS SYS-57 resource release), THEN
    `sink.record(ContainerHealthEvent { action_taken: Destroy,
    ... })`, THEN returns the structured error. The ordering is
    statically required by the contract — a sink failure must not
    mask the resource release.
  * Added `pub fn observe_health<R, S>(&self, strategy_id, runtime,
    sink, observed_at_seconds) -> ContainerHealthState`. Matches
    on `ContainerHealthState`; Healthy returns the state read-only
    (no runtime mutation, no event); Unresponsive calls
    `runtime.restart(&strategy_id)` AND `sink.record(...)` in one
    transaction (SYS-13's atomic auto-restart + dashboard
    fan-out).
  * Added `pub const fn startup_deadline_millis(&self) -> u64`
    that re-exports the `atp-types` constant so callers can
    populate `deadline_millis` without reaching into `atp-types`.
  * Added 6 in-crate unit tests covering the gate happy-path,
    refusal, destroy-call assertion, no-op-on-healthy,
    auto-restart-on-unresponsive, and exactly-once-probe.
- Added `crates/atp-orchestrator/tests/orch_1_lifecycle_contract.rs`:
  * Spy implementations of both ports with per-method call
    counters and a Forbidden* sink that panics if invoked
    (matches the ERR-3 / ERR-5 / ERR-6 pattern).
  * Six integration tests anchoring the post-conditions
    behaviourally: ReadyWithinDeadline outcome + zero event,
    DeadlineExceeded refusal + destroy_calls == 1 +
    stop_calls == 0 + restart_calls == 0 + exactly one event,
    Healthy probe read-only, Unresponsive probe restart +
    event-once + zero destroy/stop, mode-uniformity (Live and
    Paper launches share envelope shape), zero-acceptance on
    refusal.
- Added `architecture/runtime_services.json` orchestrator_lifecycle_contract
  block (180 lines): types-crate + orchestrator-crate, all five
  declared enums/structs with required + forbidden fields, the
  NFR-P9 constant declaration, the two port declarations, both
  entry points with full guard metadata including:
  * launch_guard.runtime_destroy_call = "runtime.destroy"
  * launch_guard.exceeded_action_taken =
    "ContainerLifecycleAction::Destroy"
  * launch_guard.forbidden_mutations: 10 tokens (containers.insert
    / registry.add / self.spawn_container / self.suppress_event
    etc. — every plausible regression path)
  * health_observe_guard.forbidden_mutations_on_healthy: 6 tokens
    (runtime.restart / runtime.destroy / sink.record /
    self.notify_dashboard etc. — the SYS-13 selectivity invariant)
  * 6 deferred-list entries naming the concrete Docker driver,
    SRS-ORCH-002 resource-profile enforcement, SRS-ORCH-003
    workload-priority arbitration, SRS-ORCH-004 deployment-version
    surface, the concrete sink wiring, and restart back-off.
- Added `tools/orchestrator_lifecycle_check.py` (683 lines):
  * 11 static checks (lifecycle action enum, health state enum,
    launch readiness enum, three struct shape checks with
    forbidden-field allowlist, NFR-P9 constant value check, two
    port trait checks, the two entry-point guards).
  * Inline `_variant_arm` helper (not in
    `tools/_rust_parser.py` — that hoist is still tracked) so the
    check can handle struct-variant match arms (the existing
    `_match_arm` from error_handling_check only handles unit
    variants).
  * The launch guard check enforces: presence of runtime.start,
    presence of runtime.destroy, presence of sink.record,
    presence of the action_taken token, presence of the rejection
    category or factory call, ABSENCE of any forbidden_mutations
    token, AND the positional invariant `destroy_pos < sink_pos`
    (so a refactor that swaps order would be caught).
  * The observe-health guard check enforces: presence of
    runtime.health, presence of runtime.restart inside the
    Unresponsive arm, presence of sink.record inside the
    Unresponsive arm, AND ABSENCE of any forbidden mutation
    inside the Healthy arm.
  * `assert_orchestrator_lifecycle_static(config, root)` returns
    the 11-bullet evidence list for `tools/architecture_check.py`
    to consume without invoking cargo.
  * cargo smoke (`cargo test -p atp-orchestrator --lib` + the new
    integration test file) gates the final PASS bullet.
- Wired into `tools/architecture_check.py`: import the static
  helper, add `assert_orchestrator_lifecycle(config)`, and run it

Date: 2026-05-13
Feature completed: ERR-6 — IB pacing budget exceeded by configured

What I did:
- Prep commit (24391a0): extended SAFETY_PATH_RE in
  `tools/critic_check.py` to add `pacing[_-]?budget` and
  `ingestion[_-]?schedule` to the safety-path alternation. Continues
  the per-feature precedent (ERR-2 added connectivity, ERR-3 added
  stale_data, ERR-4 added subscription_limit + market_data_line in
  SESSION 16 commit 8143ac5, ERR-5 added ingestion_validation +
  record_quarantine in SESSION 17 commit ff10ef0). The split-commit
  shape exactly mirrors SESSIONs 16 + 17.
- Feat commit (2bfa1c4):
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `IngestionPacingBudgetExceeded` variant to
    `OrderErrorCategory` (now 9 variants) with wire string
    `"INGESTION_PACING_BUDGET_EXCEEDED"` — single source of truth for
    the SyRS SYS-64 wire vocabulary; no parallel enum.
  * Added `pub struct IngestionJobRequest { job_kind: String,
    window_seconds: u64 }` — vendor-neutral schedule envelope.
    Deliberately omits broker / IB session / tick / vendor-dataset /
    vendor-table / parquet-path / credential fields (caught by the
    contract block's 7-element forbidden_fields allowlist).
  * Added `pub enum PacingBudgetState { WithinBudget, BudgetExceeded }`
    with `const is_exceeded()` helper. 2-state cadence mirrors ERR-4's
    SubscriptionLimitState.
  * Added `pub struct PacingBudgetEvent { state, job_kind,
    projected_requests: u32, permitted_requests: u32,
    observed_at_seconds: u64 }` — exactly five fields, no
    broker/session/vendor/tick leakage. Carrying BOTH projected AND
    permitted closes a TOCTOU window (same rationale as ERR-4's
    current_lines + configured_limit). `job_kind` semantically encodes
    the window (minute-bar-watchlist → SYS-22b overnight,
    option-chain-capture → SYS-23 near-close), so no separate
    window_label field.
  * Added `pub struct StructuredPacingError { category, error_type,
    message, original_request: IngestionJobRequest }` with a
    category-pinned factory `budget_exceeded(request, projected,
    permitted)` that `debug_assert!`s the category stays
    `OrderErrorCategory::IngestionPacingBudgetExceeded`. Implements
    `fmt::Display` and `std::error::Error`. Message format:
    `"SRS-DATA-002 + SRS-DATA-004 + SyRS SYS-55: ingestion job <kind>
    over pacing budget — projected <N> requests, permitted <M>"`.
  * Added 5 new unit tests: PacingBudgetState predicate,
    IngestionJobRequest + PacingBudgetEvent exhaustive destructures
    (forbidden-field proofs), TOCTOU pairing assertion (projected
    >= permitted on BudgetExceeded), factory wire-string + Display
    round-trip. Total atp-types unit tests: 25 (was 20 in SESSION 17).
  * Extended the existing
    `order_error_category_wire_strings_track_syrs_sys_64` test to
    cover the 9th variant.
- Extended `crates/atp-data/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub trait PacingBudgetValidator` with three read-only
    methods: `projected_requests`, `permitted_requests`,
    `check_budget`. The trait has NO mutator method — the
    zero-job-start invariant is anchored at the port shape so a
    concrete validator cannot dispatch the job through the probe
    call.
  * Added `pub trait PacingBudgetEventSink { fn record(&self, event:
    PacingBudgetEvent); }`. Concrete sinks (deferred) route events
    to logs, the dashboard scheduling-view alert pane, and the
    notification dispatcher per SyRS SYS-55's "until scope or window
    configuration is reduced" clause.
  * Added `pub struct IngestionJobScheduled { job_kind: String }` —
    only construction site is the `WithinBudget` arm of
    `schedule_ingestion_job`.
  * Added `DataLayer::schedule_ingestion_job<V, S>(schedule,
    validator, events, observed_at_seconds) -> Result<
    IngestionJobScheduled, StructuredPacingError>` with the match:
    `WithinBudget => Ok(IngestionJobScheduled { ... })`,
    `BudgetExceeded => { let projected =
    validator.projected_requests(&schedule); let permitted =
    validator.permitted_requests(&schedule); events.record(
    PacingBudgetEvent { ... });
    Err(StructuredPacingError::budget_exceeded(schedule, projected,
    permitted)) }`. Takes NO `StrategyMode` parameter — SyRS SYS-55
    applies the same pacing-budget rule independent of which strategy
    is live; the scheduled ingestion jobs precede mode selection.
  * Added `#[doc(hidden)] pub const _PACING_BUDGET_CATEGORY:
    OrderErrorCategory = OrderErrorCategory::IngestionPacingBudgetExceeded;`
    workspace-level reference to the canonical wire-string source.
    Mirrors ERR-4's `_SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_CATEGORY` and ERR-5's
    `_INGESTION_VALIDATION_CATEGORY`.
  * Added 3 new in-crate unit tests: WithinBudget happy path with
    `PacingBudgetForbiddenSink`, BudgetExceeded rejection with one
    event, validator call-count sanity (CountingValidator wrapper
    asserts check_budget probed once + projected/permitted each read
    once on the rejection leaf). Total atp-data unit tests: 7 (was 4
    in SESSION 17).
- Added `crates/atp-data/tests/err_6_pacing_budget_blocked.rs`
  (L7 domain integration test, 5 tests, ~456 lines):
  * `PacingBudgetValidatorSpy` (parameterized state + projected +
    permitted + per-method call counters), `PacingBudgetEventSinkSpy`
    (collects events), `PacingBudgetForbiddenSink` (panics on
    `record`) for cross-state isolation.
  * `err_6_budget_exceeded_state_blocks_job_with_structured_error` —
    full ERR-6 contract: category, wire string, message trace
    strings (SRS-DATA-002, SRS-DATA-004, SYS-55, job_kind, projected,
    permitted), exactly one event recorded with all five fields,
    validator probed once for `check_budget` and once each for
    `projected_requests` / `permitted_requests`.
  * `err_6_within_budget_state_returns_scheduled_and_emits_no_event`
    — positive control with `PacingBudgetForbiddenSink` panic stub.
    Validator probed for `check_budget` only (numerics methods must
    not be read on the accept path).
  * `err_6_budget_exceeded_state_holds_across_many_schedules` —
    pseudo-property sweep over 5 cases mixing both SyRS SYS-55 jobs
    (SYS-22b minute-bar watchlist + SYS-23 option-chain capture); per-
    case projected/permitted numerics match.
  * `err_6_identical_contract_for_minute_bar_and_option_chain_jobs`
    — SyRS SYS-55 job-invariance: rejection envelope is byte-identical
    for minute-bar-watchlist and option-chain-capture (category +
    error_type + wire string equal across jobs; original_request and
    message differ by design — they carry the per-call payload).
  * `err_6_budget_exceeded_anchors_zero_job_start_via_port_shape` —
    PacingBudgetValidator trait exposes no mutator, so the gate
    cannot start a job through the public port API. Primary
    enforcement is the static check's 14-pattern
    `forbidden_mutations` allowlist; this Rust test anchors the
    behavioral post-condition.

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- **Concrete PacingBudgetValidator implementation deferred.** The
  gate is wired-but-empty until a concrete validator lands that
  projects watchlist size × per-symbol request granularity against
  the IB pacing tier (SYS-31's 60-requests-per-10-minute ceiling)
  for both windows. Same wired-but-empty shape ERR-2..5 shipped
  under. Owner: SRS-DATA-002 + SRS-DATA-004 + the orchestrator-side
  scheduler config. When that lands, it plugs into the existing
  schedule_ingestion_job gate without changing the gate's signature.
- **Dashboard alert + notification fan-out deferred.** SyRS SYS-55
  requires alerting the operator at scheduling time with scope-
  reduction guidance — the gate emits one structured event per
  refused job (correct semantics for fan-in); the dashboard/
  notification side is downstream. Owner: SRS-NOTIF-001 +
  SRS-LOG-001.
- **SyRS SYS-31 15-second-identical-request runtime throttle out of
  scope.** That clause is a runtime concern (during the actual IB
  historical-data adapter call), not a scheduling-time concern.
  ERR-6's gate runs at scheduling time and refuses over-budget
  jobs; the 15-second throttle belongs on the IB adapter request
  path. Owner: SRS-DATA-002 + SRS-DATA-004 adapter implementation.
  Explicitly listed in the contract's `deferred` array.
- **Shared-parser hoist still deferred.** SESSION 16 flagged the
  hoist into `tools/_rust_parser.py` when the 5th ERR-* feature
  reused the parsers. ERR-5 was the 5th, ERR-6 is now the 6th
  (after error_handling, connectivity, freshness, subscription_limit,
  ingestion_validation). A `TODO(post-hoist)` comment in `tools/
  pacing_budget_check.py` next to the three imports flags it for
  the next session. The hoist itself is a single refactor commit
  (move 5 helpers + update 5 import statements + add a one-line
  entry to the shared parser doc).
- **`/codex:adversarial-review` skill still unavailable.** Same as
  SESSION 17 — the skill isn't surfaced in the user-invocable list
  (only codex:setup, codex:rescue, codex:gpt-5-4-prompting,
  codex:codex-cli-runtime, codex:codex-result-handling are
  exposed), so the judgment-pass critic ran via the AGENTS.md
  fallback path: a fresh-context general-purpose subagent given
  `prompts/critic_prompt.md` + the staged diff. Worked identically
  to the primary path; same JSON schema, same approve/warn/block
  rules. If a future session has the Codex skill available,
  prefer the primary path — the judgment pass benefits from
  Codex's git tooling for large diffs (this session's feat commit
  was 2192 LOC inserted).
- **Vendor literal hygiene held.** Same precedent as ERR-5 — neutral
  source names (`minute-bar-watchlist`, `option-chain-capture`) used
  throughout test fixtures and source strings. The
  `forbidden_fields` allowlist on IngestionJobRequest and
  PacingBudgetEvent still names vendor-specific literals
  (databento_dataset, sharadar_table, raw_parquet_path,
  vendor_credentials) as field names to reject — those are JSON /
  Python / SRS-doc strings, not in scanned src/ files, so they're
  fine where they sit.

=== SESSION 17 ===
Date: 2026-05-13
Feature completed: ERR-5 — Ingestion record validation failure:
quarantine records that fail any of the six SyRS SYS-77 rules (a..f)
at the DataLayer layer, publish a structured IngestionValidationEvent
carrying the QuarantineReason for downstream count-and-nature
aggregation, and produce zero write to the primary storage tier on
the failure path (traces SRS-DATA-013 + SyRS SYS-77 + StRS SN-1.26 /
SN-1.27).
Status: 103 remaining features

What I did:
- Prep commit (ff10ef0): extended SAFETY_PATH_RE in
  `tools/critic_check.py` to add `ingestion[_-]?validation` and
  `record[_-]?quarantine` to the safety-path alternation. Continues
  the per-feature precedent (ERR-2 added connectivity, ERR-3 added
  stale_data, ERR-4 added subscription_limit + market_data_line in
  SESSION 16 commit 8143ac5). The split-commit shape exactly mirrors
  SESSION 16's workflow.
- Feat commit (40fef50):
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `IngestionRecordValidationFailed` variant to
    `OrderErrorCategory` (now 8 variants) with wire string
    `"INGESTION_RECORD_VALIDATION_FAILED"` — single source of truth
    for the SyRS SYS-64 wire vocabulary; no parallel enum.
  * Added `pub struct IngestionRecordSubmission { source: String,
    record_hash: String }` — vendor-neutral envelope. Deliberately
    omits broker / IB session / tick / vendor-dataset / vendor-table /
    parquet-path / credential fields (caught by the contract block's
    7-element forbidden_fields allowlist).
  * Added `pub enum QuarantineReason` — Copy/Hash/PartialEq/Eq 6-
    variant enum mapping 1:1 to the SyRS SYS-77 rules (a..f):
    RangeViolation, OhlcOutOfBand, NegativeVolume, NullRequiredField,
    DuplicateRecord, OptionFieldMissing. SCREAMING_SNAKE wire strings
    via `as_str()`. Copy + Hash so dashboards can aggregate by reason
    via a HashMap key without scanning a string.
  * Added `pub enum RecordValidationOutcome { Valid,
    Quarantined(QuarantineReason) }` with `is_quarantined()` helper.
    2-state cadence mirrors ERR-4's WithinLimit/ExceededLimit; reason
    is carried in-band as a payload (clean separation of state vs.
    reason — different from a flat 7-variant enum).
  * Added `pub struct IngestionValidationEvent { state, reason,
    source, record_hash, observed_at_seconds }` — exactly five
    fields, no broker/session/vendor/tick leakage. `state` and
    `reason` are redundant by design (mirrors ERR-4's state +
    numerics) so sinks don't need to destructure the outcome.
  * Added `pub struct StructuredIngestionError { category,
    error_type, message, original_record: IngestionRecordSubmission }`
    with a category-pinned factory `quarantined(record, reason)` that
    `debug_assert!`s the category stays
    `OrderErrorCategory::IngestionRecordValidationFailed`. Implements
    `fmt::Display` and `std::error::Error`. Message format:
    `"SRS-DATA-013 + SyRS SYS-77: record <hash> from <source>
    quarantined — <REASON_WIRE_STRING>"`.
  * Added 5 new unit tests: new variant's wire string, all six
    QuarantineReason wire strings, RecordValidationOutcome
    predicate, IngestionRecordSubmission + IngestionValidationEvent
    exhaustive destructures (forbidden-field proofs), factory
    wire-string + Display round-trip. Total atp-types unit tests:
    20 (was 15 in SESSION 16).
- Extended `crates/atp-data/src/lib.rs` (was a 26-line stub; now ~245
  lines including unit tests):
  * Added `pub trait RecordValidator { fn validate(&self, record:
    &IngestionRecordSubmission) -> RecordValidationOutcome; }`. The
    trait has NO mutator method — the zero-write-to-primary
    invariant is anchored at the port shape so a concrete validator
    cannot commit a record through the probe call.
  * Added `pub trait IngestionValidationEventSink { fn record(&self,
    event: IngestionValidationEvent); }`. Concrete sinks (deferred)
    route events to logs, the dashboard WebSocket alert pane, and
    the notification dispatcher per SyRS SYS-77's alert clause.
  * Added `pub struct IngestionAccepted { source, record_hash }` —
    only construction site is the `Valid` arm of `ingest_record`.
  * Added `DataLayer::ingest_record<V, S>(record,
    validator, events, observed_at_seconds) -> Result<IngestionAccepted,
    StructuredIngestionError>` with the match:
    `Valid => Ok(IngestionAccepted { ... })`,
    `Quarantined(reason) => { events.record(IngestionValidationEvent
    { ... }); Err(StructuredIngestionError::quarantined(record,
    reason)) }`. Takes NO `StrategyMode` parameter — SyRS SYS-77
    applies the same six rules uniformly across every ingestion
    source.
  * Added `#[doc(hidden)] pub const _INGESTION_VALIDATION_CATEGORY:
    OrderErrorCategory = OrderErrorCategory::IngestionRecordValidationFailed;`
    as a workspace-level reference to the canonical wire-string
    source. Mirrors `_SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_CATEGORY` in atp-market-data.
  * Added 3 new in-crate unit tests: Valid happy path with
    ForbiddenSink-panic stub, Quarantined rejection with one event,
    validator-call-count sanity (CountingValidator wrapper, asserts
    validate is probed exactly once per record). Total atp-data
    unit tests: 4 (was 1 in SESSION 16).
- Added `crates/atp-data/tests/err_5_record_validation_blocked.rs`

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- **Concrete RecordValidator implementation deferred.** The gate
  is wired-but-empty until a concrete RecordValidator lands.
  Same wired-but-empty shape ERR-3 and ERR-4 shipped under.
  Owner: SRS-DATA-001..006 + SRS-DATA-013 (the six SyRS SYS-77
  rules need actual implementations against equity OHLCV bars
  and option-chain records). When that lands, it plugs into the
  existing ingest_record gate without changing the gate's
  signature.
- **Quarantine storage backend deferred.** SyRS SYS-77 requires
  rejected records to be persisted "in a separate store"; the
  gate emits a record_hash but the full payload goes to
  storage. Owner: SRS-DATA-014 / SRS-DATA-015. When that lands,
  it consumes the IngestionValidationEvent stream from a
  concrete IngestionValidationEventSink implementation.
- **Notification dispatcher fan-out deferred.** SyRS SYS-77
  alert clause requires "count and nature of quarantined
  records" — the count is an aggregation property the sink
  layer computes. Owner: SRS-NOTIF-001 / SYS-77 alert clause.
  The gate emits one event per quarantined record (correct
  semantics for fan-in).
- **Shared-parser hoist still deferred.** SESSION 16 flagged
  the hoist into `tools/_rust_parser.py` when the 5th ERR-*
  feature reused the parsers. ERR-5 is that 5th feature (after
  error_handling, connectivity, freshness, subscription_limit).
  A `TODO(session-17+)` comment in `tools/
  ingestion_validation_check.py` next to the three imports
  flags it for the next session. The hoist itself is a single
  refactor commit (move 5 helpers + update 4 import statements
  + add a one-line entry to the shared parser doc).
- **`_quarantined_arm` local helper.** ERR-5's match has a
  payload-binding pattern (`Quarantined(reason) =>`) that the
  shared `_match_arm` regex can't match literally. Added a
  local helper `_quarantined_arm(body, variant_token)` that
  finds the variant followed by `(...)` and extracts the arm
  body via the same brace/paren-balanced scan. If a sixth
  ERR-* feature uses a payload-bound variant, consider
  promoting the helper to the shared parser module alongside
  the SESSION 16 hoist.
- **Vendor literal hygiene.** The dependency-boundary checker
  (`tools/dependency_boundary_check.py`) and the deterministic
  critic's `adapter-isolation:vendor-import` rule both grep-
  scan `crates/atp-data/**` (the dep-boundary check scans
  `src/` only; the deterministic critic scans the whole crate
  tree including `tests/`). The initial drafts of the new
  types + gate + integration test used vendor-name source
  strings (`"databento-equity-bars"`, `"sharadar-fundamentals"`),
  which tripped both checks. Resolved by switching to
  neutral source names (`"bulk-equity-bars"`,
  `"fundamental-records"`) consistent with SyRS terminology
  (SYS-22a "bulk equity data provider", SYS-26 "fundamental
  data"). For future ERR-* features that touch ingestion or
  any path under `crates/atp-data/**`, lead with neutral
  source names from the first draft. The `forbidden_fields`
  allowlist on `IngestionRecordSubmission` and
  `IngestionValidationEvent` still names the vendor-specific
  literals to reject as field names (databento_dataset,
  sharadar_table, raw_parquet_path, vendor_credentials) —
  those are JSON / Python / SRS-doc strings, not in
  scanned src/ files, so they're fine where they sit.
- **`/codex:adversarial-review` skill unavailable in this
  session.** The skill isn't surfaced in the user-invocable
  list (only codex:setup and codex:rescue are exposed), so
  the judgment-pass critic ran via the AGENTS.md fallback
  path: a fresh-context general-purpose subagent given
  `prompts/critic_prompt.md` + the staged diff. Worked
  identically to the primary path; same JSON schema, same
  approve/warn/block rules. If a future session has the
  Codex skill available, prefer the primary path — the
  judgment-pass benefits from Codex's git tooling for large
  diffs (this session's feat commit was 2155 LOC inserted).

=== SESSION 16 ===
Date: 2026-05-12
Feature completed: ERR-4 — Market-data line limit exceeded: reject the
subscription request with SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_REACHED at the
MarketDataSubscriptionManager layer, publish a structured
SubscriptionLimitEvent carrying both current_lines AND configured_limit
for dashboard fan-out, and produce zero mutation on the subscription
registry (traces SRS-MD-002 + SyRS SYS-70 + SyRS SYS-64 identical-
contract + StRS A-13 ~100-line ballpark)
Status: 104 remaining features

What I did:
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub struct SubscriptionRequest { strategy_id, symbol }` —
    the source-neutral request envelope the manager gates on
    (mirrors OrderSubmission minus quantity, since a subscription has
    no order semantics).
  * Added `pub enum SubscriptionLimitState { WithinLimit, ExceededLimit }`
    with a `const is_exceeded()` helper. ExceededLimit types the
    SRS-MD-002 / SYS-70 rejection path.
  * Added `pub struct SubscriptionLimitEvent { state, strategy_id,
    symbol, current_lines: u32, configured_limit: u32 }` — exactly five
    fields, no broker/session/vendor/tick leakage. Carrying BOTH
    current_lines AND configured_limit closes a TOCTOU window: the
    configured value can be re-tuned between rejection and dashboard
    render, so the event is self-describing.
  * Added `pub struct StructuredSubscriptionError { category:
    OrderErrorCategory, error_type, message, original_request:
    SubscriptionRequest }` with a category-pinned factory
    `limit_reached(request, current, limit)` that constructs the
    rejection envelope and `debug_assert!`s the category stays
    `OrderErrorCategory::SubscriptionLimitReached`. Reuses the
    pre-declared OrderErrorCategory variant as the single source of
    truth for the SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_REACHED wire string (no parallel
    enum — that would be a SYS-64 invariant violation waiting to
    happen the next time someone adds a category).
  * Added 4 new unit tests: WithinLimit / ExceededLimit predicate
    coverage, `SubscriptionLimitEvent` exhaustive destructure (proves
    no extra public fields), StRS A-13 current_lines + configured_limit
    sanity (~100-line ballpark), and the factory wire-string + Display
    round-trip. Total atp-types unit tests: 15 (was 11 in SESSION 15).
- Extended `crates/atp-market-data/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub trait SubscriptionLineCounter { fn lines_in_use(&self)
    -> u32; fn line_limit(&self) -> u32; fn try_acquire(&self, request:
    &SubscriptionRequest) -> SubscriptionLimitState; }`. The port owns
    the line accounting (concrete impl backed by
    `ATP_MARKET_DATA_LINE_LIMIT` and the live subscription set is
    deferred to SRS-MD-001 / SRS-MD-007). `try_acquire` is read-only
    with respect to the registry — admission happens after the manager
    observes `WithinLimit`.
  * Added `pub trait SubscriptionLimitEventSink { fn record(&self,
    event: SubscriptionLimitEvent); }`. Concrete sinks (later) route
    events to logs (SRS-LOG-001), the dashboard WebSocket alert pane
    (SyRS SYS-70's "alert the operator on the dashboard" clause), and
    the notification dispatcher.
  * Added `pub struct SubscriptionAccepted { strategy_id, symbol }` as
    the happy-path envelope. The static check pins it as the only
    construction site inside the WithinLimit arm.
  * Added `MarketDataSubscriptionManager::request_subscription<C, S>(...)
    -> Result<SubscriptionAccepted, StructuredSubscriptionError>` with
    the match: `WithinLimit => Ok(SubscriptionAccepted { ... })`,
    `ExceededLimit => { current = counter.lines_in_use();
    limit = counter.line_limit(); events.record(SubscriptionLimitEvent {
    ... });
    Err(StructuredSubscriptionError::limit_reached(request, current,
    limit)) }`. The gate takes NO `StrategyMode` parameter — SyRS SYS-64
    mandates an identical error contract for live and paper modes, and
    SyRS SYS-70 places the gate over the consolidated subscription set
    for all active strategies regardless of mode.
  * Added `#[doc(hidden)] pub const _SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_CATEGORY:
    OrderErrorCategory = OrderErrorCategory::SubscriptionLimitReached;`
    as a workspace-level reference to the canonical wire-string source
    so a future dead-code scan cannot drop the link.
  * Added 3 new in-crate unit tests: WithinLimit happy path with
    forbidden-sink-equivalent, ExceededLimit rejection with one event,
    and a counter-call-count sanity test proving `try_acquire` is
    consulted exactly once per request. Total atp-market-data unit
    tests: 4 (was 1 in SESSION 15).
- Added `crates/atp-market-data/tests/err_4_subscription_limit_blocked.rs`
  (L7 domain integration test, 5 tests):
  * `LineCounterSpy` (parameterized state + current_lines +
    configured_limit + per-method call counters), `EventSinkSpy`
    (collects every recorded event), `ForbiddenSink` (panics on
    `record()`) for cross-state isolation.
  * `err_4_exceeded_state_blocks_request_with_structured_error` — full
    ERR-4 contract: error category is `SubscriptionLimitReached`, wire
    string `"SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_REACHED"`, exactly one event recorded
    with `state == ExceededLimit`, `current_lines == 100`,
    `configured_limit == 100`, correct strategy_id and symbol; counter
    probed exactly once for try_acquire / lines_in_use / line_limit.
    Message asserts trace strings (SRS-MD-002, SYS-70, strategy,
    symbol, limit value).
  * `err_4_within_limit_state_returns_accepted_and_emits_no_event` —
    negative control with the `ForbiddenSink` panic stub: WithinLimit
    must accept and must NOT record an event; counter probed for
    try_acquire only (the WithinLimit leaf doesn't populate an event,
    so lines_in_use / line_limit must not be read).
  * `err_4_exceeded_state_holds_across_many_requests` — pseudo-property
    sweep across 5 (strategy, symbol, current_lines, configured_limit)
    cases including ranges [100..9999], paper and live strategy_ids:
    zero acceptances, exactly 5 events with per-case current_lines and
    configured_limit correctly recorded; try_acquire probed exactly
    `cases.len()` times.
  * `err_4_identical_contract_for_live_and_paper_subscribers` — SYS-64
    invariant: the rejection envelope is byte-identical for a
    strategy_id naming a live strategy and one naming a paper strategy
    (category + error_type + wire string equal across modes;
    original_request and message differ by design — they carry the
    per-caller payload). Two events recorded with identical state and
    numerics, only strategy_id differing.
  * `err_4_exceeded_state_anchors_zero_mutation_via_port_shape` — the
    zero-registry-mutation invariant anchored at the port-shape level:
    the SubscriptionLineCounter trait exposes NO mutator method, so
    the manager cannot move the in-use count through the public port
    API. The PRIMARY enforcement is the static check's
    `forbidden_mutations` allowlist (13 patterns: registry.insert / add
    / push, subscriptions.insert / push / add, request.acquire,
    counter.acquire / commit / reserve, lines.increment, self.register,
    self.add_subscription); this Rust test anchors the behavioral
    post-condition. (Renamed from
    `err_4_exceeded_state_does_not_mutate_subscription_registry` after
    the judgment-pass critic flagged the original assertion as
    tautological — see Critic verdicts below.)

      were addressed before commit 1 landed (zero-mutation L7 test
      renamed to anchor port-shape semantics rather than the
      previously-tautological before-after counter snapshot; the
      contract's `forbidden_mutations` allowlist extended from 6 to
      13 patterns).
  COMMIT 2 (chore(critic) — 8143ac5):
    deterministic: APPROVE — 0 findings
    judgment: would BLOCK by rule `meta:critic-self-modification`
      (the literal refusal clause #4 in `prompts/critic_prompt.md`).
      Per the autonomous-agent workflow, only humans bypass this
      meta-block; the operator explicitly signed off via the
      AskUserQuestion "Split into two commits" path. The block is
      unconditional by design — it is the gate's reviewer-facing
      trigger for changes to itself. The override is recorded in the
      commit message and here so shell history and commit metadata
      both carry the audit trail.

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- **ERR-4b (deferred):** SRS-MD-002 also requires the line-limit
  gate to fire when an order is placed against a symbol with no
  existing subscription — `submit_live_order` would acquire a line
  via the subscription manager and surface `SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_REACHED`
  through the existing `StructuredOrderError` envelope (which is
  why the variant is pre-declared in `OrderErrorCategory`). This
  adds another port to `submit_live_order`'s signature (now at five
  ports; would become six). Next session should:
  (a) introduce `LiveSubscriptionAcquirer` (or similar) at the
      execution layer with a method that delegates to the subscription
      manager;
  (b) thread it through `submit_live_order` as a sixth port
      reference, nested inside the existing Connected + Fresh leaf
      (the deepest happy path);
  (c) extend `tools/error_handling_check.py` (or its peer) with a
      static check that the order-submission path also produces
      `SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_REACHED` when the line-limit gate fails;
  (d) add an `err_4b_*` integration test in
      `crates/atp-execution/tests/`;
  (e) add a new feature_list.json entry for ERR-4b (it does not
      currently exist).
- **Concrete `SubscriptionLineCounter` impl** wired to
  `ATP_MARKET_DATA_LINE_LIMIT` and the live subscription set. The
  actual bookkeeping (the set of open lines, dedup of multi-strategy
  subscriptions to the same symbol per SyRS SYS-70) belongs to
  SRS-MD-001 / SRS-MD-007. ERR-4 ships only the port shape and the
  gate; SRS-MD-001 plugs in the concrete state holder.
- The `request_subscription` signature now takes two port references
  (counter + events). Any future feature that adds a new
  subscription-manager guard (e.g., rotation / priority queuing per
  StRS A-13 if the line limit is over-subscribed) should follow the
  same pattern: introduce a port trait at the market-data layer,
  extend the signature, and nest the new match inside the appropriate
  existing arm.
- The `OrderErrorCategory::SubscriptionLimitReached` variant is now
  consumed by `atp-market-data` via the
  `StructuredSubscriptionError::limit_reached` factory and a hidden
  `_SUBSCRIPTION_LIMIT_CATEGORY` const. The constant guards against a
  future dead-code scan dropping the link between the wire string and
  this crate. If a third caller emerges (likely ERR-4b at
  atp-execution), consider promoting the constant out of `doc(hidden)`
  or hoisting a shared helper.
- The `error_type` field for the rejection is
  `"SubscriptionLimitReached"` (CamelCase, like ERR-2's
  `"IbGatewayUnreachable"` and ERR-3's `"MarketDataStale"`). The
  SESSION 14 note about avoiding snake_case tokens inside core crates
  still applies: `market_data` could collide with the SRS-ARCH-002
  dependency-boundary regex if a future error_type uses it.
- `tools/subscription_limit_check.py` reuses `_trait_body` from
  `tools/connectivity_check.py`, `_struct_body` / `_enum_body` from
  `tools/historical_data_check.py`, and `_fn_block` / `_match_arm`
  from `tools/error_handling_check.py`. As of this session, four
  per-feature checkers share these parsers (`error_handling_check`,
  `connectivity_check`, `freshness_check`,
  `subscription_limit_check`). If a fifth ERR-* feature needs them
  (likely ERR-6 for the IB pacing budget port), strongly consider
  hoisting `_fn_block` / `_match_arm` / `_struct_body` / `_enum_body`
  / `_trait_body` into a shared helper module
  (e.g. `tools/_rust_parser.py`).
- The ExceededLimit-leaf message string contains the symbol and the
  strategy_id (e.g. `"AAPL"` and `"live-alpha-1"`). Both are
  operator-visible identifiers, not PII / secrets — the ERR-1 /
  ERR-2 / ERR-3 messages already include both, so this is consistent
  with the established pattern. The message also surfaces the
  configured limit value (e.g. `"100"`) which is operator-set
  configuration, not sensitive data.
- The judgment-pass `block` on commit 2 is a permanent feature of
  the gate, not a one-off. Any future change to `tools/critic_check.py`
  or `prompts/critic_prompt.md` will trip the same rule. The
  established procedure (split into two commits, AskUserQuestion
  sign-off, record the override in the commit message + progress.txt)
  is the workflow.

Date: 2026-05-11
Feature completed: ERR-3 — Market data stale: reject live order
submission with MARKET_DATA_STALE, publish a structured StaleDataEvent
carrying the observed staleness in seconds, do NOT request a reconnect
(staleness is a data-side condition, not a transport fault), and

SYS-64 / SYS-87 / NFR-P5 15s threshold)
Status: 105 remaining features

What I did:
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub enum MarketDataFreshness { Fresh, Stale }` with a
    `const is_stale()` helper. `Stale` types the SRS-MD-004 /
    SyRS SYS-39a stale-data state.
  * Added `pub struct StaleDataEvent { state: MarketDataFreshness,
    strategy_id: StrategyId, symbol: String, staleness_seconds: u64 }`
    — exactly four fields, no broker / session / vendor / tick
    identifiers. The `staleness_seconds` scalar lets dashboards and
    the notification dispatcher surface how stale the feed actually
    got before the gate fired.
  * Added 3 new unit tests: `is_stale` coverage of the two states,
    `StaleDataEvent` exhaustive-destructure (proves no extra public
    fields exist), and an NFR-P5 above-15s sanity check. Total
    atp-types unit tests: 11 (was 8 in SESSION 14).
- Extended `crates/atp-execution/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub trait MarketDataFreshnessProbe { fn freshness(&self,
    symbol: &str) -> MarketDataFreshness; fn staleness_seconds(&self,
    symbol: &str) -> u64; }`. The port lives at the execution layer
    so the data-freshness gate is observable from execution without
    pulling `atp-execution` into a dependency on `atp-market-data`
    (SRS-ARCH-002). The eventual subscription-manager implementation
    will own the heartbeat timestamps, sequence-gap tracking, and
    the configurable threshold.
  * Added `pub trait StaleDataEventSink { fn record(&self, event:
    StaleDataEvent); }`. Concrete sinks (later) route events to logs
    (SRS-LOG-001), the dashboard WebSocket, and the notification
    dispatcher.
  * Changed `ExecutionEngine::submit_live_order` signature to take
    five port references: `broker: &B`, `connectivity: &C`,
    `events: &E`, `freshness: &F`, `stale_events: &S`. The
    `StrategyMode::Live` Connected sub-arm now nests a match on
    `freshness.freshness(&submission.symbol)`:
    `MarketDataFreshness::Fresh => broker.submit_order(submission)`
    is the happy path. `MarketDataFreshness::Stale =>` reads
    `staleness_seconds`, pushes a `StaleDataEvent` through
    `stale_events.record(...)`, then returns
    `Err(StructuredOrderError { category: MarketDataStale,
    error_type: "MarketDataStale", message: "...SRS-MD-004 + NFR-P5
    15s + observed Xs", original_order: submission })`. The broker
    port is NOT invoked on the Stale leaf, AND
    `connectivity.request_reconnect()` is NOT called (staleness is a
    data-side condition, not a transport fault).
  * Updated all 4 existing in-crate unit tests to thread
    `AlwaysFresh` (panics on `staleness_seconds`) / `ForbiddenFreshness`
    (panics on both methods) / `RecordingStaleEvents` (collects every
    recorded event) stubs through. Added 1 new unit test:
    `live_submission_is_blocked_when_market_data_is_stale` with a
    parameterized `StubFreshness` exercising the 22s staleness path.
    Total atp-execution unit tests: 7 (was 6 in SESSION 14).
- Updated `crates/atp-execution/tests/err_1_no_ib_side_effect.rs` to
  thread `AlwaysFresh` + `ForbiddenFreshness` + `StaleEventSinkSpy`

  (broker, connectivity, connectivity events, freshness, stale
  events). Any future feature that adds a new guard (ERR-4
  line-limit, ERR-6 IB pacing, ERR-7 / ERR-8 liquidation timeouts)
  should follow the same pattern: introduce a port trait at the
  execution layer, extend the signature, and nest the new match
  inside the appropriate existing arm. ERR-4 (line-limit) and
  ERR-6 (pacing) most naturally nest inside Connected + Fresh.
  ERR-7 / ERR-8 (kill-switch / hot-swap liquidation timeouts) are

  `_enum_body`. Not urgent — there are only two callers today.

  Symbols are operator-visible identifiers, not PII / secrets — the
  ERR-1 and ERR-2 messages already include the strategy ID, so this
  is consistent with the established pattern. If a future feature

  strategy.

=== SESSION 14 ===
Date: 2026-05-11
Feature completed: ERR-2 — IB Gateway unreachable: reject live order
submission with CONNECTIVITY_BLOCKED, publish a structured
ConnectivityEvent, attempt reconnection, and produce zero IB order side
effect (traces SRS-SAFE-003 + SRS-MD-005 + SyRS SYS-45 / SYS-46 / NFR-R2)
Status: 106 remaining features

What I did:
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub enum ConnectivityState { Connected, Unreachable,
    ScheduledRestartWindow }` with a `const is_blocked()` helper. The
    `Unreachable` variant types the SRS-SAFE-003 connectivity-loss
    state; `ScheduledRestartWindow` types the SRS-MD-005 daily-restart
    suspension state.
  * Added `pub struct ConnectivityEvent { state: ConnectivityState,
    strategy_id: StrategyId, symbol: String, scheduled_restart: bool }`
    — exactly four fields, no broker / session / vendor identifiers.
    The `scheduled_restart` flag is true iff the state is
    `ScheduledRestartWindow` so dashboards and the notification
    dispatcher can apply SRS-MD-005's suppression rule without
    re-inspecting the enum.
  * Added 3 new unit tests: `is_blocked` coverage of the three states,
    `ConnectivityEvent` exhaustive-destructure (proves no extra public
    fields exist), and the SRS-MD-005 suppression-flag round-trip.
- Extended `crates/atp-execution/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub trait BrokerageConnectivity { fn state(&self) ->
    ConnectivityState; fn request_reconnect(&self); }`. The port lives
    at the execution layer so the gate is observable from execution
    without pulling `atp-execution` into a dependency on
    `atp-adapters` (SRS-ARCH-002).
  * Added `pub trait ConnectivityEventSink { fn record(&self, event:
    ConnectivityEvent); }`. Concrete sinks (later) route events to
    logs, the dashboard WebSocket (ALERTS / ACCOUNT_STATUS), and the
    notification dispatcher.
  * Changed `ExecutionEngine::submit_live_order` signature to take
    three port references: `broker: &B`, `connectivity: &C`, `events:
    &E`. The `StrategyMode::Live` arm now nests a match on
    `connectivity.state()`. `ConnectivityState::Connected =>
    broker.submit_order(submission)` is the happy path.
    `Unreachable | ScheduledRestartWindow =>` builds a
    `ConnectivityEvent` (with the `scheduled_restart` flag computed
    via `matches!(state, ScheduledRestartWindow)`), pushes it through
    `events.record(...)`, calls `connectivity.request_reconnect()`,
    then returns `Err(StructuredOrderError { category:
    ConnectivityBlocked, error_type: "IbGatewayUnreachable",
    message: "...SRS-SAFE-003", original_order: submission })`. The
    broker port is NOT invoked on either blocked-state path.
  * Updated the 3 existing unit tests to thread always-connected /
    forbidden-connectivity stubs through. Added 2 new unit tests:
    `live_submission_is_blocked_when_gateway_unreachable` and
    `live_submission_is_blocked_during_scheduled_restart_window`. The
    Paper-mode test now uses `ForbiddenConnectivity` (panics on any
    call) to prove ERR-1's short-circuit is independent of the ERR-2
    connectivity gate.
- Updated `crates/atp-execution/tests/err_1_no_ib_side_effect.rs` to
  thread `AlwaysConnected` + `ForbiddenConnectivity` + `EventSinkSpy`
  stubs through the existing 3 tests. The ERR-1 contract is preserved:
  Paper submissions still reject with NON_LIVE_STRATEGY_SUBMISSION and
  zero broker side effect, and the Live control test still routes
  through. All 3 tests pass under the new signature.
- Added `crates/atp-execution/tests/err_2_connectivity_blocked.rs`
  (L7 domain integration test, 4 tests):
  * `BrokerageSpy` (counts `submit_order` calls), `ConnectivitySpy`
    (parameterized initial state + counts `request_reconnect`
    invocations), `EventSinkSpy` (collects every recorded event).
  * `err_2_unreachable_state_blocks_live_submission_with_no_broker_call`
    — full ERR-2 contract: error category is `ConnectivityBlocked`,
    wire string is `"CONNECTIVITY_BLOCKED"`, `broker.calls == 0`,
    `connectivity.reconnect_calls == 1`, exactly one event with
    `state == Unreachable` and `scheduled_restart == false`.
  * `err_2_scheduled_restart_window_blocks_with_suppressed_marker` —
    SRS-MD-005 path: same as above but with `state ==
    ScheduledRestartWindow` and `scheduled_restart == true`.
  * `err_2_connected_state_still_routes_through_broker` — negative
    control: Live + Connected reaches the broker (rejection is
    selective).
  * `err_2_unreachable_holds_across_many_live_submissions` —
    pseudo-property: sweeps 5 (strategy, symbol, qty) cases under
    Unreachable; broker spy stays at 0, reconnect spy hits exactly
    `cases.len()`, and exactly `cases.len()` events are recorded.

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- ERR-2 lands the **connectivity safety gate** at the execution
  layer. There is still no production caller of
  `submit_live_order`; the orchestrator (later feature) will wire an
  `atp-adapters` `BrokerageAdapter` to `LiveBrokerageSubmit` and an
  IB-adapter probe to `BrokerageConnectivity` +
  `ConnectivityEventSink`. The gate is observable from execution
  without `atp-execution` depending on `atp-adapters`.
- The `submit_live_order` signature now takes three port references.
  Any future feature that adds a new guard (ERR-3 stale market data,
  ERR-4 line-limit, ERR-6 IB pacing, ERR-7 / ERR-8 liquidation
  timeouts) should follow the same pattern: introduce a port trait at
  the execution layer, extend the signature, and add the
  corresponding match arm inside the existing `StrategyMode::Live`
  branch. The progress.txt SESSION 13 note about "Each later ERR-*
  feature should add its own match arm" still applies.
- The `error_type` field for the connectivity rejection is
  `"IbGatewayUnreachable"` (CamelCase, distinct from the forbidden
  `ib_gateway` snake_case token that the SRS-ARCH-002 dependency
  boundary forbids inside core crates). The dependency check is
  case-sensitive substring, so `IbGateway` is safe; future ERR-*
  error_type strings should also stay in CamelCase to keep the
  dependency boundary regex green.
- `tools/connectivity_check.py` introduces a `_trait_body` helper
  that parses `pub trait <name> { ... }` bodies. If a third ERR-*
  feature needs to pin trait methods, the helper can be promoted to
  a shared module alongside `_enum_body` / `_struct_body` /
  `_fn_block` / `_match_arm`.
- Pre-existing dirty/untracked files unrelated to ERR-2:
  `.devserver.log`, `.devserver.pid`, `.claude/`, `.vscode/`,
  `prompts/coding_prompt.md`, `prompts/initializer_prompt.md`,
  `.critic_report.json` (the staged-diff JSON output of the
  deterministic critic — generated by this session, OK to keep or
  delete). They were not reverted.

  ERR-4..ERR-9, then SRS-API-001 and beyond.

Feature completed: ERR-1 — Order submitted by a non-live strategy to

What I did:
- Extended `crates/atp-types/src/lib.rs`:
  * Moved `OrderSubmission` + `OrderReceipt` here from
    `atp-adapters` so both `atp-execution` (sender) and
    `atp-adapters` (impl side) share one definition without
    `atp-execution` depending on `atp-adapters` (dependency-direction
    rule: adapters and execution are siblings, both deps of types).
    Kept `pub use atp_types::{OrderReceipt, OrderSubmission}` in
    `atp-adapters` so existing callers compile unchanged.
  * Added `pub enum StrategyMode { Live, Paper }` with const
    `is_live()` — types the single-live-strategy designation
    (SRS-EXE-001 / SyRS AC-15).
  * Added `pub enum OrderErrorCategory` with 7 variants:
    `InvalidSymbol`, `InsufficientBuyingPower`,
    `ConnectivityBlocked`, `RateLimited`, `MarketDataStale`,
    `SubscriptionLimitReached`, `NonLiveStrategySubmission`. Each
    variant maps via `as_str()` to its SyRS SYS-64 upper-snake wire
    string (`"NON_LIVE_STRATEGY_SUBMISSION"` etc.) so the form is
    identical across Rust / Python / REST / WebSocket.
  * Added `pub struct StructuredOrderError { category, error_type,
    message, original_order }` — exactly the four fields
    SRS-ERR-001 requires, no broker/vendor identifier fields. Impl
    `Display` (renders `[CATEGORY] error_type: message`) + `Error`.
- Extended `crates/atp-execution/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub trait LiveBrokerageSubmit { fn submit_order(...) ->
    Result<OrderReceipt, StructuredOrderError>; }`. The port lives
    at the execution layer; adapters do not implement it directly —
    the orchestrator (later feature) wires an adapter to it. This
    keeps `atp-execution` free of any dep on `atp-adapters`.
  * Added `ExecutionEngine::submit_live_order<B: LiveBrokerageSubmit>
    (&self, mode: StrategyMode, submission: OrderSubmission, broker:
    &B) -> Result<OrderReceipt, StructuredOrderError>` with a `match
    mode` whose `StrategyMode::Live` arm is the ONLY call site of
    `broker.submit_order(...)`. The `StrategyMode::Paper` arm
    returns `Err(StructuredOrderError { category:
    NonLiveStrategySubmission, error_type:
    "NonLiveLiveRouteBlocked", message: "strategy `{id}` is not the
    designated live strategy...SRS-EXE-001", original_order:
    submission })` BEFORE any broker call, so a Paper submission can
    never produce an IB order side effect.
  * Added 4 new unit tests in the same crate: routing happy path,
    paper-rejection with `broker.calls == 0` post-condition, the
    structured error display format, plus the existing boundary
    test was retained.
- Added `crates/atp-execution/tests/err_1_no_ib_side_effect.rs`
  (L7 domain integration test, 3 tests):

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- ERR-1 lands the **rejection vocabulary** only. The live IB
  routing pipeline (real submit, lifecycle state machine,
  correlation-ID idempotency, IB-pacing handling) lands with
  later EXE-* features. The brokerage port
  `LiveBrokerageSubmit` is defined at the execution layer; the
  orchestrator (later) wires an `atp-adapters` brokerage adapter
  to it. Right now no production code path constructs an impl
  of `LiveBrokerageSubmit` — only the test spy does. That is
  intentional: ERR-1's contract is "if such a port exists, a
  Paper submission can never invoke it."
- `OrderSubmission` and `OrderReceipt` now live in `atp-types`
  with a `pub use` re-export from `atp-adapters`. Any future
  feature that imports these types directly from
  `atp_adapters::` will keep working, but new code should
  prefer `atp_types::{OrderSubmission, OrderReceipt}` to make
  the dependency direction explicit.
- The structured-error vocabulary intentionally covers all 7
  SyRS SYS-64 categories (not just `NonLiveStrategySubmission`)
  so that ERR-2..ERR-9 can land without revisiting `atp-types`.
  Each later ERR-* feature should add its own match arm
  (mapping `AdapterError::*` → `OrderErrorCategory::*`) inside
  the corresponding execution-engine guard (connectivity,
  staleness, pacing, market-data-line limit, ingestion
  validation, hot-swap liquidation, kill-switch liquidation,
  startup config).
- `tools/error_handling_check.py` reuses `_struct_body` /
  `_enum_body` from `historical_data_check.py` (no copy-paste),
  matching the API-6 / API-7 import pattern. The check also
  introduces a `_fn_block` helper and a `_match_arm` helper
  that parses match arms with brace + string-literal awareness.
  Future ERR-* contract checks can promote these to a shared
  helper if more arms need pinning.
- The "no broker call outside Live arm" check is regex-based.
  A regression that hides the broker call behind a helper
  function call (e.g. `self.really_route(broker, submission)`)
  inside the Paper arm would pass the static check. The L7
  spy-adapter integration test is the runtime defense for this
  failure mode — the spy counts every call regardless of how
  it is reached.
- The `error_type` field in the Paper-arm error is
  `"NonLiveLiveRouteBlocked"`. If a later feature finds this
  string awkward, it can be renamed without touching the
  contract; only the *category* is part of the SRS-ERR-001
  wire vocabulary.
- Pre-existing dirty/untracked files unrelated to ERR-1:
  `.devserver.log`, `.devserver.pid`, `.claude/`, `.vscode/`,
  `prompts/coding_prompt.md`, `prompts/initializer_prompt.md`.
  They were not reverted (consistent with prior sessions).
- No features were skipped for clarification this session.
- Lowest remaining P1 by ID is ERR-2 (IB Gateway unreachable),
  then ERR-3..ERR-9 (stale market data, market-data line limit,
  ingestion validation, IB pacing, Hot-Swap liquidation timeout,
  kill-switch liquidation timeout, missing/invalid startup
  config), then SRS-API-001 and beyond.

What I did:
- Extended `crates/atp-adapters/src/lib.rs`:
  * Added `pub enum AssetClass { Equity, Option, Future, Etf, Index }`
    (Phase 1 SRS-DATA-007 universe).

    FullyAdjusted, TotalReturn }` per SRS-DATA-012 (the four
    normalization modes options strategies / indicators / benchmarks

    `normalization_mode: NormalizationMode` fields so the unified
    request shape carries every API-7 description capability.
  * Added `pub struct HistoricalQueryResult { symbol, asset_class,
    normalization_mode, bars }` — the source-neutral envelope returned
    by every provider. Deliberately does NOT carry `provider`,
    `vendor`, `source`, `source_provider`, or `data_source` — the
    contract check refuses any of those.
  * Changed `HistoricalDataAdapter::historical_data` return type from
    `AdapterResult<Vec<HistoricalBar>>` to
    `AdapterResult<HistoricalQueryResult>` so every consumer of the
    unified interface sees the same envelope.

    `unified_historical_query_carries_asset_class_and_normalization`
    (round-trips every (AssetClass, NormalizationMode) pair through
    every Phase 1 historical provider — 5 × 4 = 20 pairs),
    `historical_query_result_envelope_is_source_neutral` (exhaustive

- API-7 declares the unified historical query contract surface only —
  every `HistoricalDataAdapter::historical_data` call still returns
  `NotConfigured`. Real ingestion behaviour lands with DATA-1

  corporate actions, schema evolution).

  `AdapterResult<HistoricalQueryResult>` instead of
  `AdapterResult<Vec<HistoricalBar>>`. This is a breaking change to
  the trait surface — downstream features that build on the trait
  must construct the envelope (symbol + asset_class +
  normalization_mode + bars) and not just bars.

  `tools/adapter_check.py::_trait_block` directly (no copy-paste),
  matching the API-6 import pattern. The new check tool also has its
  own `_struct_body` and `_enum_body` brace-matching helpers —
  future contract checks for new envelope-style result types
  (e.g. factor outputs) should consider promoting them to a shared
  helper.
- The Python protocol-method matcher in
  `tools/historical_data_check.py` deliberately skips single-line
  `def get_bars(...)` matches inside docstrings (doctest examples)
  by requiring a newline inside the parameter list. If a future
  refactor inlines the Protocol method onto a single line, the check
  will need to be relaxed.

Date: 2026-05-06
Feature completed: API-4 — operator CLI surface for kill switch,
strategy management, live designation, Hot-Swap, readiness status,
and basic administration (traces SRS-API-001 + SRS-SAFE-001)
Status: 111 remaining features

What I did:
- Added a new Python package `python/atp_cli/` that is the declarative
  source of truth for the operator CLI:
  * `commands.py` defines `Group` (6 buckets: kill-switch, strategy,
    live, hot-swap, readiness, admin), `ExitCode` (OK=0,
    USAGE_ERROR=2, CONFIRMATION_REQUIRED=3, NOT_FOUND=4, NOT_READY=5,
    TIMEOUT=6, NOT_IMPLEMENTED=64), frozen-slots `Argument` and
    `Command` dataclasses, the 18-entry `COMMANDS` tuple, and the
    access-policy constants `ACCESS_MODEL=local-shell`,
    `AUTH_MODEL=local-single-user`, `CLI_ENTRY_POINT=atp`. Each
    command carries `srs_refs`, `arguments`, `exit_codes`, and
    `requires_confirmation`. Four commands are confirmation-gated
    (kill-switch activate, strategy rollback, live promote,
    hot-swap trigger).
  * `manual.py` builds a deterministic JSON manual dict from
    `COMMANDS` (pure stdlib), with per-group `x-srs-refs`, per-command
    `x-srs-refs`/`x-requires-confirmation`, and document-level
    `x-access-model`/`x-auth-model` extensions encoding SRS-SEC-002.
  * `manual.json` is the frozen byte-equal snapshot.
  * `runner.py` builds an argparse parser from `COMMANDS`, exposes
    `python -m atp_cli --list` for surface introspection, enforces
    --confirm on irreversible commands (exit 3 on miss), and exits
    with NOT_IMPLEMENTED (64) for every stub handler.
  * `__main__.py` wires `python -m atp_cli`.
  * `__init__.py` re-exports the 17-name public surface.
  * `README.md` summarises access model, the 6-group/18-command
    table, exit codes, sample invocations, and snapshot regeneration.
- Added `tools/cli_check.py` mirroring `rest_api_check.py` and
  `websocket_api_check.py`: same exit-code contract, evidence-bullet
  output, `--update` flag. 11 checks total: 6 per-group (assert SRS
  refs, required commands, --confirm gating where applicable),
  `confirmation_invariant` (every irreversible command declares
  --confirm and CONFIRMATION_REQUIRED), `local_shell_policy`
  (constants + manual x-extensions), `exit_code_contract` (every
  command exit_codes ⊆ documented ExitCode and includes OK),
  `manual_snapshot` (byte-equality), `runner_smoke` (subprocess
  exercises --list, kill-switch activate without --confirm → exit 3,
  with --confirm → exit 64).
- Extended `architecture/runtime_services.json` with a `cli` block
  listing the 6 required groups, the manual snapshot path, the entry
  point, the access/auth policy, and the four confirmation-required
  commands. Extended `tools/architecture_check.py` with
  `assert_cli(config)` so the surface is enforced architecturally —
  `SRS-ARCH-001 PASS` now adds an `atp_cli covers 6 groups and runs
  atp via local-shell (local-single-user)` evidence line.
- Wired `python3 tools/cli_check.py` into `init.sh` between the
  WebSocket API check and the deployment check; `✓ Environment ready`
  now requires the new check too.
- Added `tests/test_cli.py` (15 tests across 10 classes): subprocess
  contract test, command shape walk, group coverage (== set(Group),
  len 6, len(COMMANDS) == 18), confirmation invariant for the four
  irreversible commands, manual snapshot byte-equality, determinism,
  manual JSON parse, local-shell policy, exit-code contract, runner
  subprocess (list / confirm gating / NOT_IMPLEMENTED stub / readiness
  stub), parser build, commands_by_group, public-docstring walk.
- Tightened `tests/test_architecture.py` SRS-ARCH-001 aggregate test
  to require the new `atp_cli covers 6 groups` and `local-shell`
  evidence in the architecture-check output.
- Extended `architecture/README.md` with an `API-4` section
  documenting the direct check command, snapshot update recipe, and
  the parallel relationship to API-2/API-3.

  serves the placeholder `python3 -m http.server`.
- The CLI runner deliberately returns ExitCode.NOT_IMPLEMENTED (64)
  for every executable command. Downstream features should keep this
  exit code reserved for missing handlers and use the documented
  codes (OK, NOT_FOUND, NOT_READY, TIMEOUT, ...) for real outcomes.
- `requires_confirmation=True` commands MUST also document
  `ExitCode.CONFIRMATION_REQUIRED` and declare a `--confirm` argument
  with `required=True`. The check enforces all three at once; do not
  weaken any one of them without revisiting SRS-SAFE-001 / UI-4.

  scripts table). Operators invoke via `python -m atp_cli`. When a
  packaging step lands, set `[project.scripts] atp = "atp_cli.runner:main"`.
- `init.sh` is now stricter again: a broken `atp_cli` import or a
  missing manual snapshot fails init. Recover via
  `python3 tools/cli_check.py --update` or by running
  `python3 tools/cli_check.py` directly to see the failure.

  `prompts/initializer_prompt.md`, `prompts/coding_prompt.md`,

  not reverted.

  may not apply directly since adapter interfaces are Rust traits —
  consider surfacing them through a contract check that scans
  `crates/atp-adapters/src/` for the required trait methods.

=== SESSION 8 ===
Date: 2026-05-05
Feature completed: API-3 — WebSocket API contract surface for live
dashboard updates (P&L, metrics, account status, heartbeat, logs,
alerts, Reservoir ranking, strategy state)
Status: 112 remaining features

What I did:
- Added a new Python package `python/atp_ws/` that is the declarative
  source of truth for the operator WebSocket API:
  * `channels.py` defines `Direction`, `MessageType` (7 frames),
    `Channel` (8 buckets: PNL, METRICS, ACCOUNT_STATUS, HEARTBEAT,
    LOGS, ALERTS, RESERVOIR_RANKING, STRATEGY_STATE), frozen-slots
    `EventChannel` and `ClientCommand` dataclasses, the 8-entry
    `EVENT_CHANNELS` tuple, and the 3-entry `CLIENT_COMMANDS` tuple
    (SUBSCRIBE, UNSUBSCRIBE, HEARTBEAT_PING). `BIND_HOST=127.0.0.1`,
    `AUTH_MODEL=local-single-user`, `WS_PATH=/ws/v1`,
    `MAX_REFRESH_SECONDS=5` (NFR-P2 ceiling). Each channel carries
    `srs_refs`, `payload_fields`, `refresh_seconds` (0 means
    event-driven for LOGS/ALERTS), `requires_subscription`.
  * `asyncapi.py` builds a deterministic AsyncAPI 2.6 dict from
    EVENT_CHANNELS + CLIENT_COMMANDS (pure stdlib), with per-channel
    `subscribe` operations carrying `x-srs-refs`, `x-refresh-seconds`,
    `x-direction`, plus a multiplexed `/ws/v1/_control` channel for
    the SUBSCRIBE/UNSUBSCRIBE/HEARTBEAT_PING commands. Document-level
    `x-bind-host`/`x-auth-model`/`x-ws-path` extensions encode
    SRS-SEC-002.
  * `asyncapi.json` is the frozen byte-equal snapshot regenerated from
    `EVENT_CHANNELS`/`CLIENT_COMMANDS`.
  * `__init__.py` re-exports the 17-name public surface.
  * `README.md` summarises auth model, channel table with refresh
    cadence, message types, sample subscribe/event JSON, and snapshot
    regeneration recipe.
- Added `tools/websocket_api_check.py` mirroring `rest_api_check.py`:
  same exit-code contract, evidence-bullet output, `--update` flag.
  13 checks total: 8 per-channel (assert SRS refs, required payload
  fields, subscription required), `subscribe_protocol` (SUBSCRIBE +
  UNSUBSCRIBE both accept `channels` and reply ACK),
  `heartbeat_protocol` (HEARTBEAT_PING ↔ HEARTBEAT_PONG and traces
  SYS-39), `refresh_budget` (every channel within
  [0, MAX_REFRESH_SECONDS=5]s — NFR-P2), `asyncapi_snapshot`
  (byte-equality), `loopback_policy` (constants + x-extensions).
- Extended `architecture/runtime_services.json` with a `websocket_api`
  block listing 8 required channels, the AsyncAPI snapshot path,
  bind/auth/ws-path/refresh-ceiling policy. Extended
  `tools/architecture_check.py` with `assert_websocket_api(config)` so
  the surface is enforced architecturally — `SRS-ARCH-001 PASS` now
  adds an `atp_ws covers 8 channels and binds 127.0.0.1 /ws/v1
  (local-single-user)` evidence line.
- Wired `python3 tools/websocket_api_check.py` into `init.sh` between
  the REST API check and the deployment check; `✓ Environment ready`
  now requires the new check too.
- Added `tests/test_websocket_api.py` (13 tests across 6 classes):
  subprocess contract test, EventChannel shape walk, channel
  coverage (== set(Channel), len 8), AsyncAPI snapshot byte-equality,
  determinism, AsyncAPI 2.6.0 parse, loopback policy, x-extensions,
  subscribe protocol, heartbeat protocol, NFR-P2 refresh budget,
  public-docstring walk.
- Tightened `tests/test_architecture.py` SRS-ARCH-001 aggregate test
  to require the new `atp_ws covers 8 channels` and `/ws/v1` evidence
  in the architecture-check output.
- Extended `architecture/README.md` with an `API-3` section
  documenting the direct check command, snapshot update recipe, and
  the parallel relationship to API-2 (`atp_api`).

Known issues / notes for next agent:
- API-3 declares the contract only — no real WebSocket runtime exists
  yet. Concrete publishers (PNL/METRICS/HEARTBEAT/etc.) land with
  EXE-1, ORCH-1, MD-1, RESV-1, LOG-1, NOTIF-1. `init.sh` still serves
  the placeholder `python3 -m http.server`.
- Backtest-progress streaming is intentionally NOT a WebSocket channel.
  Backtest results are served by REST `GET /api/v1/backtests/{id}`
  (API-2). If a future feature needs streaming backtest progress,
  add a new `Channel.BACKTEST_PROGRESS` bucket and bump the snapshot.
- LOGS and ALERTS use `refresh_seconds=0` to mean *event-driven, no
  fixed cadence*. The check enforces the closed interval [0, 5]; do
  not tighten the lower bound to >0 without revisiting the contract.
- The control-plane (`/ws/v1/_control`) channel is a single AsyncAPI
  channel that carries a `oneOf` of three command messages
  (SUBSCRIBE/UNSUBSCRIBE/HEARTBEAT_PING). Per-command operationIds and
  response-message tags are encoded in `x-response-message`.
- `init.sh` is now stricter: a broken `atp_ws` import or a missing
  AsyncAPI snapshot fails init. Recover via
  `python3 tools/websocket_api_check.py --update` or by running
  `python3 tools/websocket_api_check.py` directly to see the failure.

  `prompts/initializer_prompt.md`, `prompts/coding_prompt.md`,
  `Cargo.lock`, `requirements.txt`, `.claude/`. They were not
  reverted.

=== SESSION 7 ===
Date: 2026-05-05
Feature completed: SRS-ARCH-005 - Configuration system for credentials,
storage paths, IB account settings, market-data line limits, resource
limits, and notification channels
Status: 113 remaining features

What I did:
- Added a top-level `configuration` block to
  `architecture/runtime_services.json` cataloguing 16 required keys
  across the six SRS-ARCH-005 categories (credentials, storage_paths,
  ib_account, market_data_limits, resource_limits, notification_channels).
  Each key carries name, category, type (int|float|path|secret|enum|host),
  validator hints (min/max, non_empty, absolute, choices), default,
  secret flag, and SRS trace.
- Added five new resource-limit env vars to close the SyRS SYS-57/58
  gap that previously lived only as static compose labels:
  ATP_LIVE_STRATEGY_MEM_MB=512, ATP_LIVE_STRATEGY_CPU=0.25,
  ATP_PAPER_STRATEGY_MEM_MB=300, ATP_PAPER_STRATEGY_CPU=0.10,
  ATP_HOST_MEMORY_SAFETY_MARGIN_MB=2048. They are threaded through
  `.env.example`, `init.sh` defaults, the `x-atp-env` anchor in
  `docker-compose.yml`, and the existing
  `deployment.required_env_vars` list (which deployment_check.py now
  validates at the compose layer).
  IMPORTANT: the env vars are deliberately NOT substituted into the
  strategy-runtime service's `deploy.resources.limits` block. Compose's
  `memory:` field requires a unit suffix (e.g. `512M`); a raw integer
  silently means *bytes* and would OOM at boot. The compose block
  remains the static template default; the orchestrator (SRS-ORCH-002,
  future feature) reads the env vars at per-strategy clone time.
- Added a new Python package `python/atp_config/` (pure stdlib):
  * `schema.py` — `Category`, `KeyType`, `Severity` enums; `KeySpec`
    and `ReadinessFailure` dataclasses; `ReadinessReport` with `ok`,
    `errors`, `warnings`, `as_json_lines()`. `REQUIRED_KEYS` is loaded
    from runtime_services.json at import time so the JSON catalogue is
    the single source of truth.
  * `validate.py` — `load_and_validate(env, *, atp_env=None)` returning
    a structured `ReadinessReport`. Per-type validators: int/float
    parse + range; path non-empty + absolute; host non-empty;
    secret non-empty; enum choices. Production-mode escalation: a
    placeholder secret is a *warning* in development and a hard *error*
    when ATP_ENV is staging/production, so init.sh dev defaults still
    pass while staging/production cannot start with placeholders.
  * `__init__.py` re-exports the public surface (15 names).
  * `README.md` documents the categories, every key, validation rules,
    and the readiness-failure JSON-line shape (covers the
    "documented" half of the SRS-ARCH-005 AC).
- Added `tools/config_check.py` mirroring the
  `tools/deployment_check.py` pattern: same exit-code contract,
  evidence-bullet output, --fixture flag (modes:
  `missing-credential`, `placeholder-secret-in-production`,
  `invalid-line-limit`, `missing-resource-limit`,
  `invalid-storage-path`), and an `assert_configuration_static()`
  aggregator entry that `tools/architecture_check.py` consumes.
- Wired `assert_configuration_static` into `tools/architecture_check.py`
  after the SRS-ARCH-004 deployment evidence, so the aggregate
  `SRS-ARCH-001 PASS` output now ends with a
  `SRS-ARCH-005 configuration system evidence:` bullet group with one
  line per category.
- Wired `python3 tools/config_check.py` into `init.sh` after the
  deployment-check step. `✓ Environment ready` now requires the
  configuration check to pass.
- Added `tests/test_configuration.py` (24 tests): catalogue shape,
  validator behaviour for every type, structured-failure shape,
  JSON round-trip, public-docstring walk, placeholder constant
  matches `.env.example`.
- Added 5 cases to `tests/test_architecture.py`
  (positive + 4 negative fixtures) and tightened the SRS-ARCH-001
  assertion to require the SRS-ARCH-005 evidence header.
- Extended `docs/DEPLOYMENT.md` with a `## Configuration system
  (SRS-ARCH-005)` section listing all 16 keys by category, the
  validation rules, the structured failure schema, the
  staging/production placeholder-escalation rule, and the explicit
  note that compose-substitution into deploy.resources.limits is
  deliberately avoided. Added an `SRS-ARCH-005` section to
  `architecture/README.md` with the direct check command and the
  five negative fixtures.
